Organizational Content of the Southwest Political Affairs Council 71

Authorities Plan to Establish Pacification Office Under the Political Affairs Council

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the establishment of the unified government, the Guangzhou National Government and the Central Party Headquarters have been successively abolished. However, in the southwest, according to the resolutions of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Guangzhou [Kuomintang Central Executive Committee], it is planned to still establish three organizations in Guangdong: the Southwest Executive Department of the Central Party Headquarters, the Southwest Political Affairs Council, and the Southwest Military Council. The organizational laws have been drafted and submitted to the government for record. It is reported that the government has only approved the registration of the Political Affairs Council for the three organizations, and the Military Council is not to be discussed. The authorities believe that the military and political affairs of the southwestern provinces cannot be without a command organization to coordinate the pacification and suppression of bandits. Now that the Military Council has not been approved for registration, and the pacification command cannot be without a unified organization, it is planned to change the method and form a Southwest Pacification Office under the Political Affairs Council. The office can directly command the southwestern provinces to handle the pacification and suppression of bandits. The organizational law is currently being drafted by the Guangdong and Guangxi military authorities and will be submitted for discussion at the next meeting of the Political Affairs Council. The organizational regulations of the Southwest Political Affairs Council are as follows: (Article 1) The National Government, in accordance with the resolutions of the Fourth National Congress [of the Kuomintang], establishes the Southwest Political Affairs Council, which is directly under the National Government, to supervise and direct the following administrative and auditing matters within the southwestern region: (1) Internal affairs, (2) Military affairs, (3) Finance, (4) Transportation, (5) Industry, (6) Education, (7) Judicial administration. (Article 2) The Southwest Political Affairs Council of the National Government has jurisdiction over the southwestern provinces. (Article 3) The Southwest Political Affairs Council may, with the resolution of the Political Affairs Conference, increase or abolish various agencies. (Article 4) The Southwest Political Affairs Council is composed of 15 to 27 members, specially appointed, and designates 5 to 7 members as standing committee members. (Article 5) The Southwest Political Affairs Council of the National Government establishes a secretariat, with one secretary-general, specially appointed; 5 to 7 secretaries, specially appointed or recommended; 2 to 5 section chiefs, recommended; and several section clerks, appointed. (Article 6) The Political Affairs Council establishes an audit office, with one director, specially appointed; 5 to 7 auditors, specially appointed or recommended; 8 to 12 assistant auditors, 6 to 10 investigators, recommended; 16 to 20 clerks, 9 to 12 scribes, appointed. (Article 7) The Southwest Political Affairs Council of the National Government may establish 9 to 12 specialized committee members, specially appointed or recommended. (Article 8) The Political Affairs Council holds a political affairs meeting once a week, with standing committee members taking turns as chairmen. (Article 9) The following matters shall be resolved by the Political Affairs Conference: (1) Appointment and dismissal of administrative, judicial, and auditing officials above the level of recommended appointment; (2) Matters that cannot be resolved between provinces; (3) Matters concerning budgets and final accounts; (4) Other matters deemed by laws and regulations or the standing committee members to be submitted for resolution. (Article 10) The Political Affairs Council may issue orders and single-line rules within the scope of its jurisdiction, without conflicting with central laws and regulations. (Article 11) Resolutions of the Political Affairs Council shall be submitted to the National Government for review and sent to the Executive Yuan or Control Yuan for record. (Article 12) If a dispute arises between the Political Affairs Council and the central yuan [Executive, Legislative, Judicial, Examination, Control] or ministries in terms of authority, it shall be submitted to the National Government for resolution. (Article 13) The Secretary and the Director of the Audit Office may attend the political affairs meetings of this committee. (Article 14) The rules of procedure for the political affairs meetings of this committee and the organizational regulations of the Secretariat and Audit Office shall be determined separately. (Article 15) If there are any matters not fully covered in these regulations, they may be submitted to the National Government for amendment. (Article 16) These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation. (January 15)

Sun Lianzhong's Troops Withdraw to Western Fujian 72

Shantou Correspondence: The Northwest Army's Sun Lianzhong's troops, consisting of nine regiments, totaling approximately 15,000 soldiers, are complete with five branches of the military: infantry, artillery, cavalry, and engineers. They also have a great sword unit of 1,500 men and 1,200 cavalry horses. Last year, they were ordered to enter Jiangxi to suppress bandits and then garrisoned the Fuzhou and Eastern Jiangxi areas. In the past three months, the central government's supplies have been insufficient, so the division has been raising funds locally. During the New Year, they moved from Fuzhou to Shicheng and Ruijin, and on the 6th, they all arrived in Changting City, seeking food in various counties in Western Fujian. Because the division moved freely into Fujian, there has been considerable suspicion from the outside world. Yesterday, Zhong Guanxun, deputy commander of the newly formed 1st Independent Brigade in Wuping County, Fujian Province, came to Shantou to request the allocation of bullets and the provision of salaries to strengthen the Fujian-Guangdong border defense. After arriving in Shantou, Zhong stayed at the Jintai Inn on Wan'an Street. The reporter made a special trip to interview him about the recent situation on the Fujian border. According to him, last month, the Red bandits led by Peng Dehuai and others sneaked into Yunmenling and disturbed Guikeng, Dayangqiao, and Shanghang Fengshi in Wuping. The brigade launched an attack and fought fiercely in Guikeng for half a day, capturing more than 100 guns and four light machine guns. After this setback, the bandits dared not invade again. On the 28th of last month, the Red bandits in Changting invaded Guanzhuang in Shanghang, and were also defeated by Zhong Guanxun's troops, killing more than 100 bandits. Changting is currently garrisoned by Sun Lianzhong's troops, whose attitude is unclear. They have approximately 17,000 to 18,000 soldiers. They do not fly any flags and do not indicate whether they are surrendering to the Reds or resisting the Reds. In Changting, they only care about raising funds and do not take any action. However, the Western Fujian gentry have posted many welcome slogans for Sun's troops. The Lu Xinming Brigade, stationed in Liancheng and Qingliu, is withdrawing to the Yong'an and Shaxian areas in Northern Fujian. At present, the defense of Western Fujian is very serious. Zhong came here specifically to report to Commander Zhang in Shantou to request the provision of military supplies. It is understood that the commander of the newly formed 1st Independent Brigade, Zhong Shaokui, concurrently serves as the commander of the 1st Regiment, the deputy commander Zhong Guanxun, concurrently serves as the commander of the 2nd Regiment, Huang Pinmei is the commander of the 3rd Regiment, and Zhong Wencai is the commander of the 4th Regiment. The brigade was originally reorganized from the Armed Self-Help Corps and the Fujian-Jiangxi Border People's Regiment. Today, it was heard that Zhong continued to receive a letter from Zhong Shaokui in Shanghang, stating that on the 4th, hundreds of Sun Lianzhong's troops invaded Xianghu in the northern district of Wuping. Zhong's troops immediately sent a team to block them. The battle was extremely fierce, and Sun's troops were finally defeated and retreated to the Changting border. This is believed to be caused by Sun's rebellious soldiers, but Sun Lianzhong's own attitude is indeed unclear. (January 13)

Songjiang 73

Water Police Rescue: Pu's Ransom Ticket, Fan Guozhong, captain of the 1st team of the Jiangsu Water Police, personally led the team leader Zhou Liancheng, inspector Gu Laisheng, Shen Boquan, Yao Yuangeng, etc., each leading a patrol boat, encountered bandits opening fire in the Zhoucangjing area of ​​the 8th district of Fengxian this month. That night was a deep fog, and it was too late to pursue them. Suzhou 74

A Large Number of Refugees Arrive in the City and Countryside: Yesterday (21st), more than 300 refugees from Xiang arrived in the Chexie area of ​​Su Township, traveling on more than 20 boats. The resident Pan Police Team was ordered to deport them. In addition, yesterday (21st) evening, more than 40 refugees arrived outside Qimen in the city. Army Engineers to Build Roads, Work to Begin on Time: The Wuxian County's construction of the ring road around the city has been approved by the Jiangsu Construction Department. The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held on the 25th.

Each County Sets Up Water and Land Inspection Stations: Division Commander Shen of the 60th Division stationed in Suzhou believes that during the winter defense period, the bandit atmosphere in each county is not calm. Therefore, in the division's defense areas, such as Wuxian, Wujiang, Qingpu, Changshu, Wuxi, Changzhou, Piaoyang, Yixing, and Danyang, 11 counties each set up a water and land traffic inspection station. Each station has one director and three investigators. The director is the highest military officer stationed in the area, and the investigator is appointed by the director.

Wujiang 75

Another Major Robbery Case Near Yanmu: Yan Huiqing, a wine merchant in Zhang Ao Township, Yanmu County, is a man of modest means. A few days ago, a money shop in Nanxun hired a boat to send 5,000 yuan to Yan's house. The bandits learned of this. At 10:00 PM that night, more than ten bandits suddenly came, holding two long and short guns. After landing, the bandits went up to the house and into the house, beating Yan and his wife with guns, forcing them to ask where the silver was stored. Yan, suffering from severe injuries, could only tell them. The bandits broke open the silver box, and the 6,000 yuan inside was stolen. They also destroyed the boxes and cabinets in the room, and stole many clothes and ornaments. After the robbery, they fled with shouts. Upon inspection, the loss was nearly 10,000 yuan, and the victim was seriously injured. The case has been reported to the county for arrest.

Wuxi 76

Record of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Industry inviting chambers of commerce from various counties for discussion: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Industry, having taken over the administration of industry and commerce, urgently needed to understand the situation in both sectors. Therefore, on the morning of the 20th, it invited important chambers of commerce from various counties in Jiangsu to discuss the following points raised by Director He: (1) Relief of financial problems, (2) Implementation of new weights and measures, (3) Grain management, (4) Convening a committee for industrial and commercial design. Representatives present at the meeting discussed these points in detail and reported on the state of industry and commerce in their respective regions, the impact of last year's floods, the difficulties and hardships caused by the Northeast Incident, and their hopes for the future. Director He adopted each of these points and instructed the relevant departments to handle them diligently. Finally, there was an in-depth discussion on the handling of sealed Japanese goods. After the meeting, a banquet was held at the Pin Fang Branch of the Provincial Government to entertain the representatives.

Approval of the organization of the Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce: The Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce was initiated by the chambers of commerce of 35 counties in Jiangsu Province in April of last year. Applications for permission to organize had been submitted to the provincial party headquarters, but no certificate had been issued. Recently, representatives of the county chambers of commerce discussed the business tax issue in Zhenjiang and submitted a further request to the provincial party headquarters, with representatives also going to inquire. It is now reported that the provincial party headquarters held a meeting on the afternoon of the 20th and decided to approve the organization, provided that it complies with the Commercial Association Law and obtains the consent of more than two-thirds of the chambers of commerce in the province. Staff can then be dispatched to provide guidance. Representatives of the chambers of commerce are now going to the Department of Industry to investigate. In addition to the 35 initiating counties, more than 20 chambers of commerce have joined, exceeding the statutory two-thirds. Yesterday, representatives of the chambers of commerce submitted a statement to the provincial party headquarters, stating that this requirement had been met. Once staff are dispatched to issue the certificate, it can be established soon.

County government joint trial of five kidnappers: Six bandits, Xing Youyi, Cao Jinbiao, Pan Guoliang, Yang Kunshan, Dong San, and Yin Dekui, kidnapped Yao Qibao, a partner in the Shuntai South Goods Store, and Wang Jiansan, the owner of the Xinchang Rice Store, in the Xin'an Town of the 13th district of this county. After being apprehended by the water patrol team of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, except for Yin Dekui, who was left in Shanghai for medical treatment due to injury, the remaining five bandits were escorted back to Wuxi by the local Public Security Bureau and handed over to the county government for detention and interrogation. Yesterday morning, County Chief Chen instructed Du Youlin of the political police to go to the countryside to summon the victims Yao Qibao and Wang Jiansan to identify the criminals. In the afternoon, County Chief Chen and Section Chief Wang held a joint trial. First, the victims Yao Qibao and Wang Jiansan were interrogated, followed by the five kidnappers, Xing Youyi, etc. However, Xing and the others gave slippery confessions and refused to tell the truth. Yao and Wang were then ordered to identify the suspects in court, confirming that they were the perpetrators. One of the kidnappers, Dong San, was identified as the one who disguised himself as a beggar and went to Xinchang Rice Store to negotiate the ransom. After the interrogation, Yao and Wang were ordered to return, and Xing Youyi and the others were returned to custody pending legal proceedings. During the trial, Yao Qibao also claimed that there were more than ten kidnappers in total, with four "box piers" (likely meaning firearms). They had previously engaged in two shootouts with police officers in Taihu Lake, seized a fishing boat, shot and killed the boat owner, and dumped the body in the lake before hiding the hostages. The fishing boat has been seized by the Suzhou Public Security Bureau, and the boat owner's wife is being held in Suzhou, can the county chief be requested to send an official letter to Suzhou to release her? Chen County Chief immediately said that this case would be handled separately, and that Yao could present the reason and submit it to the county for review. Yao Qibao then left the county and returned home.

Jiangyin 77

Party and government departments maintain the Jimei Pawnshop: Since the closure of the Jimei Pawnshop in the city on the 18th, the poor have been in a state of panic. Yesterday (the 19th) at 2 p.m., the party and government organs held a meeting in the county party headquarters to discuss the situation. As a result, it was decided that the Jimei Pawnshop would be responsible for maintaining operations through the lunar New Year. Gold, jewelry, silk, satin, and fur should not be sold. The party and government departments, together with the county chamber of commerce and the money industry association, will immediately investigate the total value of the pawnshop's deposits, loan amounts, and redeemed goods. All customer deposits, village loans, and redemption funds must not be used. In the evening, they also negotiated with the county chamber of commerce to raise funds for relief, with a minimum of 10,000 yuan to maintain operations through the lunar New Year. The results of the meeting will be submitted to the county government for a decision. Wu Shuying, chairman of the chamber of commerce, and Zhu Danqing will convene the money industry to raise funds to maintain the pawnshop for the benefit of the poor.

Zhenjiang 78

Deadline for clearing the remaining bandits in Fengshan: Yang, the battalion commander of the Second Battalion of the Third Regiment of Infantry of the Jiangsu Security Department, and the Fourth Battalion of the regiment, were ordered to jointly suppress the remaining bandits under Liu Shoubiao in Fengshan and other places, along with the militia groups from Zhenjiang and Jurong counties. They have sent letters to the governments of Zhenjiang and Jurong counties, requesting them to order their subordinates to cooperate in the suppression, regardless of territorial boundaries, by the 25th of this month, starting from the 11th. Fengshan and other places have now been surrounded. It is expected that the bandit leader Liu Shoubiao will be captured soon.

Yangzhou 79

Villagers kill bandits, request inspection: Two cloth sellers from Xiejiaji, in the area of Jiangyi Kunlian, were approached by two bandits with handguns yesterday morning (the 19th). The bandits first tied up the two cloth sellers and then searched them, stealing 298 yuan in cash before leaving. After the two cloth sellers managed to untie themselves, they followed the bandits. Villagers then sounded gongs and pursued the bandits with weapons, chasing them to Chenjiaji in Jiangyi County, where they killed one bandit (surnamed Xu) and captured another (surnamed Zhou). The captured bandit and the two cloth sellers were handed over to the police team stationed in the area by the villagers. The body of the killed bandit has been reported to the court, which dispatched Inspector Zong Dinghua this morning (the 20th) to conduct an inspection.

Nantong 80

The case of stealing and selling relief wheat is handed over to the judiciary: The National Government Relief Flood Relief Committee allocated 15,000 tons of American wheat to relieve flood victims in the counties along the canal. A large amount of this relief wheat was stolen and sold by boatmen while being transported from the Tianshenggang Grain Station in Nantong. The stationmaster, An Diesheng, has investigated the matter and handed over the thieves and the grain merchants who purchased the stolen wheat to the court for legal proceedings.

Banditry flares up again in the ports along the Yangtze River: The coastal ports of Nantong and Haimen counties, such as Da'an and Daming, have recently seen a resurgence of banditry after the withdrawal of the defense forces. Nearby towns have been heavily affected. Bandit ships are carrying more than 20 hostages, all kidnapped from counties south of the Yangtze River. The Nantong County government telegraphed Haimen on the 19th to send Chuhui Xun.

Automatic abolition of public security sub-bureaus in various districts: The districts of Jinle, Liuqiao, and Shigang in Nantong have automatically abolished their public security sub-bureaus because of financial difficulties, lack of firearms, and rampant extortion by police officers. The defense corps in each district have been organized. Other districts are currently in the process of doing the same.

Ningbo 81

Bandits kidnap and burn houses: Yesterday (the 19th) at 6 a.m., more than 200 bandits from Xinchang suddenly arrived at the Maojia area of Fanjieling in the Lianshan district of Fenghua, first kidnapping villager Mao Huojia. The local defense corps, upon hearing the alarm, immediately mustered more than 70 men and bravely fought the bandits fiercely for three hours. Mao Xizuo, a member of the defense corps, was killed by the bandits, and Mao Zongfa and Zhou Xingjun were seriously injured. Fearing that reinforcements would arrive soon, the bandits fled east. The bandits then looted and burned houses in Tiandun, a place five li from Fanjieling, causing heavy losses.

Bandits plot to kidnap guests, one shot: Zhu Weisheng, the village head of Minghe Village, Cibei, is relatively wealthy and employs five or six servants. The other night, seven or eight bandits, all armed with guns, broke into the house while others remained outside to guard. When the three bandits entered the house, Zhu was chatting with guest Gu Qianzhang. Zhu, seeing the bandits, quickly tried to hide. The servants also sounded gongs to gather the villagers. Seeing the situation, the bandits opened fire, hitting the guest Gu Qianzhang in the right leg. Upon hearing the alarm, hundreds of villagers gathered, and the bandits fled in panic. The villagers pursued them and captured a bandit named He Yongsheng, who was handed over to the government for investigation.

Local News

Wang Jingwei goes to Beijing yesterday 82

Mr. and Mrs. Wang boarded the train at Zhenru

Issues a statement of responsibility before leaving

After arriving in Shanghai the night before, Mr. Wang Jingwei originally planned to travel to Beijing in the same train as Sun Ke that night. However, due to his recent recovery from illness and the fatigue of the journey, he rested in Shanghai for one night. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., Mr. Wang returned to the Luo'er Hospital for an injection by Dr. Luo'er. He returned to his residence around 11 a.m., and Chu Minyi notified the railway bureau to prepare a train to go to Beijing at 3:15 p.m. The railway bureau prepared two special carriages to be attached to the first express train and waited at the station. At 2:18 p.m. yesterday afternoon, Mr. Chu arrived at the station first. At 3:15 p.m., when the train was about to depart, Mr. Wang had not yet arrived at the North Station. The railway bureau then received a phone call from Mr. Wang's residence, informing them that Mr. and Mrs. Wang, along with Tang Haian, had taken a car to Zhenru Station and asked the train to stop briefly at Zhenru for them to board. At 3:30 p.m., the train arrived at Zhenru, stopped briefly for one minute, and Mr. and Mrs. Wang and Tang Haian boarded the last special carriage to go to Beijing. Chen Xinghan, a special commissioner from the Ministry of Railways, accompanied the train to take care of everything.

Before leaving, Wang made a statement saying: (Question) Mr. Wang, what are your thoughts on meeting Mr. Chiang Kai-shek in Hangzhou? (Answer) I have not seen Mr. Chiang for several years. Although Mr. Chiang came to Shanghai several times last winter on October 21 to meet with representatives from Guangdong, due to time constraints, we did not have a detailed discussion. This time in Hangzhou, I was able to have a long meeting with Mr. Chiang. I deeply admire Mr. Chiang's sincerity and determination to unite and jointly face the national crisis. (Question) What are your thoughts on Mr. Hu Hanmin's reply telegram? (Answer) I agree with half of Mr. Hu's reply telegram and disagree with the other half. The First Plenary Session of the Central Committee decided that all Central Committee members should participate in the political conference, with Mr. Chiang, Mr. Hu, and myself as standing committee members. The responsibility of the standing committee members is to take turns chairing the meetings, and there are no other special tasks. Therefore, if the standing committee members are not in Beijing, the meeting can elect someone to be temporary chairman, as has been done before. Therefore, to say that the political conference cannot proceed without the three standing committee members is an overstatement. On this point, I share the same feeling as Mr. Hu. However, all comrades in the party are currently encouraging each other to unite sincerely and jointly face the national crisis. Therefore, considering the past rifts and striving for the present, Mr. Chiang, Mr. Hu, and myself must gather in the capital and work together to save the country. To say that we fear disagreements that would embarrass the government, and therefore should be in different places, would only make such disagreements more likely to occur. How about each of us contributing our opinions to the political conference and letting the majority decide, so that we can truly implement democracy and centralized power? This is why I cannot fully agree with Mr. Hu's reply telegram. (Question) To what extent can you do your best in Beijing this time? (Answer) I will participate in the political conference as a member of the Central Committee. In other words, I will do my best in whatever way a member of the Central Committee can. However, as my health has not fully recovered, I have agreed with my comrades that I can only attend meetings on important issues, and all other meetings, receptions, speeches, and social events will be temporarily omitted. This has been understood and agreed to by my comrades.

Lin Kanghou agrees to take the position of Vice Minister of Finance 83

Minister Huang has returned to the ministry to resume his duties

Mr. Lin agrees to make a short-term effort

According to the Guowen News Agency, Minister of Finance Huang Hanliang has returned to the ministry to work and officially resumed his duties. He immediately sent a telegram to Executive Vice Minister Lin Kanghou, urging him to take office to stabilize the market and reassure the people. At the same time, members of the banking community, upon hearing the news, also urged Mr. Lin to go to Beijing to take office. It is reported that Vice Minister Lin telegraphed Minister Huang yesterday, agreeing to make a short-term effort, and sent a telegram to President of the Executive Yuan Sun Zhesheng, which read: "To President Sun of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Kanghou previously requested that the National Government review and revoke the order appointing me as Executive Vice Minister of Finance, allowing me to retreat and avoid embarrassing myself, as I felt I was unable to assist in the ministry's affairs. This was from the sincerity and not an excuse. However, this was not approved, and I was repeatedly urged to stay. Although I dare not change my original intention, I must make a short-term effort to stabilize the market and because it is the end of the year. I still hope that you will understand my true feelings and submit another request, recommending a replacement, so as to achieve the effect of selecting talented people for government. Kanghou, in the private sector, will still contribute his wisdom for the benefit of the country and the people. I respectfully present this to you, hoping you will consider it. Lin Kanghou kowtows, Ma."

Mayor Wu hosts a reception for the diplomatic corps yesterday 84

Discusses maintaining the security of this city

Mayor Wu goes to Beijing last night

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng hosted a reception at the Cathay Hotel last night for diplomatic personnel from various countries' consulates in this city to maintain contact and discuss the issue of maintaining the security of this city. After the reception, Mayor Wu went to Beijing by night train at the summons of Chiang Kai-shek to seek instructions from the central government on the issue of maintaining security in Shanghai.

After the Japanese Riot 85

Japanese Consulate Expresses Regret to the Chinese Concession Authorities

Various Public Organizations Issue Statements Yesterday

Following the attempted arson by Japanese ruffians on the Sanyou Industrial Company's main factory the day before yesterday, resulting in the death of one Chinese constable and injuries to three others (details were reported in yesterday's newspaper), it has been learned that yesterday remained uneventful throughout the day. However, the Chinese Concession police authorities remained on high alert. The Japanese Consul expressed regret and apologized to the Chinese Concession authorities yesterday. A summary of the situation yesterday is as follows:

Japanese Consul Expresses Regret: After the incident of the Japanese riot on the previous day, Mayor Wu Tiecheng sent Secretary-General Yu to the Japanese Consulate at 3 PM to lodge a serious verbal protest, demanding a guarantee that such incidents would not recur, that the perpetrators would be severely apprehended, and reserving all rights to further negotiations. When Secretary-General Yu lodged the protest, Japanese Consul-General Murai Aoyoshi immediately acknowledged the extreme illegality of the Japanese ruffians' actions, expressed his deepest regret, and promised to severely apprehend the perpetrators. Yesterday morning at 10 AM, Consul-General Murai visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government, personally expressing his regret. He also requested Mayor Wu to severely apprehend the culprits regarding the incident a few days prior in which five Japanese monks were attacked on Ma Yu Mountain Road. Mayor Wu also expressed his agreement.

Concession Lodges Representations: During the riot by Japanese ruffians the previous morning, one Chinese constable was killed and two were wounded. In the afternoon of the same day, several Western constables were also injured in Hongkou. Following this incident, the Shanghai Municipal Council convened a board meeting at 4 PM to include the matter on the agenda. Consequently, the board deemed the lawlessness of the Japanese ruffians unimaginable concerning the Concession's security and decided that serious representations should be made to the Japanese Consulate regarding the injured and deceased police officers. Therefore, Secretary-General Fessenden was instructed to make serious representations to the Japanese Consulate. The Japanese board members present also expressed their unease and agreed to request the Japanese Consulate to strictly restrain the violent acts of the Japanese ruffians.

Japanese Consul Formally Apologizes: Following the serious representations made by the Shanghai Municipal Council, the Japanese Consulate, led by Consul-General Murai, personally visited the Council yesterday afternoon to meet with Chairman Macnaghten and formally apologized for the previous day's incident. However, it is reported that the Council has not yet fully completed all negotiations and that no proposals have been made regarding compensation for the injured and deceased Chinese constables.

Secretary-General Yu Speaks: Secretary-General Yu of the Municipal Government told a Huadong News Agency reporter yesterday that the cause of the Japanese ruffians' riot the previous morning was actually quite trivial. Several days ago, five Japanese monks were traveling through the Yinxiang Port area when they had a conflict with Chinese people, resulting in injuries. The Japanese Consulate had already approached the Municipal Government about this matter, and he had immediately agreed to apprehend and punish the culprits for the Chinese assault on the Japanese people, as the incident occurred within the Chinese territory. He also expressed his regret. However, the Japanese ruffians went so far as to kill and injure Chinese constables in the Concession and burn down the Sanyou Factory. The illegality of their actions was clearly evident. Therefore, when he protested to the Japanese Consul the previous day, he had stated that the assault on the Japanese monks and the riot were entirely separate matters, differing greatly in severity. The Municipal Government had agreed to apprehend and punish the culprits for the assault on the Japanese monks. He wondered how Japanese law would punish the riot by the Japanese ruffians. The Japanese Consul then expressed his deepest regret and personally visited the Municipal Government today to express his regret to Mayor Wu and promised to apprehend and severely punish the culprits. However, the Municipal Government has not yet submitted a formal written protest on this matter, but it is expected to be formally submitted to the Japanese Consulate tomorrow. As for the Concession authorities, he had met with Fessenden, who expressed the hope that this matter would not escalate and cause other unfortunate incidents. He did not know how negotiations would proceed.

Fessenden Speaks: A reporter from this newspaper visited Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, yesterday to inquire about the Council's attitude toward the Japanese ruffians' violent acts. Fessenden replied that the Council would make representations to the Japanese Consul-General, but a resolution could not be reached in a day or two. Fessenden also said that China and Japan were practically at war and that the public's emotions were inevitably激昂激昂. The Council's responsibility was to maintain the Concession's security to the best of its ability, without taking sides. He hoped that citizens would not overreact.

Japanese Vice-Consul Speaks: Japanese Vice-Consul Shirai Yasushi told a Huadong News Agency reporter yesterday that two major unfortunate incidents occurred in this city the day before yesterday: one was the arson by Japanese in Hudong, burning down the Sanyou Factory, and the other was the riot and disturbance caused by Japanese on North Sichuan Road. The consulate is currently investigating the perpetrators of the incidents. Several suspects have already turned themselves in, but the names are not yet ready to be released. The consular authorities believe that the actions of the Japanese residents this time were illegal and should be seriously investigated. However, the arson at the Sanyou Factory was an act of revenge. On the 18th of this month, five Japanese monks, two in monk's robes and three in plain clothes, believed that as Buddhist monks, they would not be attacked by Chinese people. Unexpectedly, when passing near the factory, they were grabbed and beaten by workers from the factory (Huadong News Agency reporter's note: Investigations at the Sanyou Factory and the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District revealed that the factory workers were completely unrelated to the incident). Two managed to escape during the confusion, while three were severely injured and remain hospitalized. It is reported that one of the injured is in critical condition. Following this incident, the Japanese residents of Shanghai were greatly angered, leading to this incident. In fact, even if the Japanese residents suffered losses, they should have appealed to the Japanese Consul to negotiate with the Municipal Government and should not have resorted to such barbaric means, causing this unfortunate incident. Consul Murai has already expressed his regret to the Municipal Government today. As for the culprits, they are being thoroughly investigated. Once apprehended, they will be severely punished. However, the consulate is concerned that relations between Chinese and Japanese residents in Shanghai have deteriorated recently, and the atmosphere is very tense. Therefore, they have decided to cable the government, requesting that warships be sent to Shanghai as a precaution.

Public Security Bureau Reports to the Municipal Government: The Public Security Bureau submitted an unofficial report to the Municipal Government yesterday, stating that at 2 AM on the 20th, the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District received a report that a fire had broken out at the Sanyou Industrial Company factory in Yinxiang Port. Wu Yuting, chief of the Fourth Precinct, immediately led police officers to the scene to provide assistance. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade also arrived to pump water and extinguish the fire, which was quickly put out, and they returned. Unexpectedly, shortly after, they heard news of another fire, suspecting a recurrence of the blaze, which was quite strange and difficult to understand. They went to the factory to investigate and found traces of damage to the fence. Upon entering, they saw that the small windows on all sides had been burned by fire, and liquor bottles were still present. They also found a large bottle with a label that read "High-Grade Beverage" (Xin Sheng News Agency reporter's note: "High-Grade Beverage" is a Japanese term, and the bottle is also a Japanese product), as well as packets of gunpowder. The factory's losses include six destroyed buildings and twenty-four damaged machines, resulting in twenty-four workers being unable to work the next day (i.e., yesterday).

Chen Constable's Condition Critical: One Chinese constable was stabbed to death by Japanese people the day before yesterday, and three other injured constables were sent to the hospital for treatment. It was reported yesterday that the most seriously injured was Chen Shengde, Constable No. 3029. Chen, a native of Anhui, 27 years old, is still unable to speak. Due to the force of the stabbing, his waist injury resulted in a severed intestine, and his left cheek was injured by gunpowder, causing him to lose a front tooth. According to visitors to the hospital, his abdomen has been operated on, but he remains unconscious. Furthermore, he lost too much blood after the incident, and his life is in danger.

Preparations to Commemorate Constable Tian: The Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District, the Eleventh Branch of the Seventh District, and other organizations are deeply saddened by the arson committed by Japanese people at the Sanyou Industrial Company factory and the shooting death of Municipal Council Chinese Constable Tian Runsheng, who bravely struggled to protect the factory. Yesterday, they initiated the organization of a memorial preparatory committee to console his spirit and published a notice seeking enthusiastic participation from various organizations. The contact address is No. 24 Shenjiazhai, Yinxiang Port.

Four Suspects Detained: Following the arson committed by Japanese people at the Sanyou Factory, all employees have been paying closer attention to their own protection. The factory has also issued a notice for security reasons that unauthorized individuals or idlers are strictly prohibited from entering. Unexpectedly, at noon, four people wearing short-sleeved clothing and resembling workers entered the factory to look around. Initially, the factory thought they were workers and paid no attention. However, their incessant questions aroused suspicion, and they were immediately detained. After questioning, Zhou Huisheng and Huishengbao were sent to the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District, while Xie Quan and Hui A'er are currently being interrogated in detail by the factory. It has been learned that Xie is a 21-year-old native of Jiangyin and a worker at Jardine Matheson, while Hui is also a native of Jiangyin and previously worked as a streetcar ticket seller. The four were traveling together out of curiosity and had no malicious intentions. After questioning, they were all sent to the Public Security Precinct.

Police Kiosk and Factory Repaired: The glass windows surrounding Police Kiosk No. 1 of the Yangshupu police station were completely destroyed by Japanese ruffians the previous morning. Yesterday, the kiosk was repaired by artisans dispatched by the police station, and the number of stationed patrol officers was larger than usual, approximately a dozen or more, including Chinese, Western, and Indian officers, with very tight security. As for all the damage to the Sanyou main factory, such as the fences and factory buildings, it was also completely repaired yesterday. A large number of public security police officers were stationed in front of the gate, and a temporary observation platform was set up in front of the dyeing room at the back of the factory to prepare for any unforeseen circumstances.

Japanese Marines Demonstrate: Near the Tianneng'an Station intersection of Tongji Road, at approximately 1:50 PM yesterday, five Japanese Marines, fully armed with rifles and ammunition, demonstrated in the area on motorcycles. The vehicles also carried portable machine guns, creating a very serious situation. Similarly, on Yokohama Road, at around 5 PM, three soldiers initially appeared, scouted around, and left. They were followed by another twenty or more, patrolling and demonstrating. Sentries were stationed outside the Japanese Marine Corps headquarters on Dixiwei Road, with very strict precautions.

Japanese Warships to Arrive in Shanghai: After this incident, the Japanese residents convened a meeting the day before yesterday and once petitioned the Japanese Consulate, also cabling the Japanese naval authorities, requesting that warships be sent to Shanghai to demonstrate. It has been learned that the Japanese side has dispatched the aircraft carrier Notoro, the cruiser Oi, and four small destroyers from the Wu Naval Port, carrying several Marines, which are en route to Shanghai and are expected to arrive here tomorrow morning. It is also learned that there are currently two Japanese warships in Shanghai: the flagship Atago and the destroyer Kamikaze. After these six ships arrive in Shanghai tomorrow, there will be a total of eight ships anchored in the Huangpu River.

Japanese Residents to Meet Tomorrow: According to the Great American Evening Post, the Japanese residents will hold a meeting at the Japanese Club on Peng Road on Saturday morning (i.e., the 23rd) to discuss the issue of what actions the residents should take if the Japanese Consul and naval commander do not take aggressive measures against China.

Chamber of Commerce's Petition: The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce petitioned the Municipal Government, stating that it was petitioning regarding a matter. The Chamber learned on the 20th of this month that Japanese ruffians had set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company's main factory and recognized that this matter concerned the safety and security of the city's commercial affairs and was very serious. It immediately sent personnel to investigate to clarify the truth and seek a resolution. According to the investigators' report, they visited the factory and spoke with Deputy Factory Director Lao, who was not present. Wang Keqiang, an employee, received them and described the incident, which was consistent with what was reported in the newspapers on the 21st. Wang then led them to visit the damaged weaving factory, which was covered in charred wood and suffered severe losses. They then went to the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District to investigate, and it was reported that evidence of the Japanese arson had been collected, including beer bottles, Japanese newspapers, and bomb fragments, which were submitted to higher authorities for review. Although the arson by Japanese ruffians at the factory was contained due to thorough temporary precautions and effective firefighting, preventing the entire factory from being burned, the Japanese's malicious plan was thwarted, but their ambition remains undeterred. It is inevitable that they will use even more vicious means against the factory in the future. Although the factory is operating normally, the workers are anxious.

Page 10

They cannot live in peace. Measures should be taken to properly protect the factory against unforeseen circumstances, and protests should be lodged with the Japanese Consul, demanding serious negotiations. The factory's location and the route taken by the Japanese ruffians for arson are indicated on the attached simplified map (map omitted), which is submitted for your review. Violent acts by Japanese ruffians in Shanghai are not new, and it has never been heard that the relevant consul has strictly enforced the law and punished them severely. Our government officials have repeatedly tolerated the situation and taken no action, leading to these individuals becoming even more reckless, resulting in the great misfortune of burning down factories and killing constables. Shanghai is an international city, the focus of global attention, and they still act without any regard, and their violent acts are escalating. The future crisis facing the factory is truly alarming. Given the lessons learned from previous incidents and the factory's remote location and the attention its successful operations have drawn from the Japanese, it is not comparable to ordinary shops and should be strictly prepared. The Municipal Government should consult with military agencies and instruct the Public Security Bureau to dispatch military police to guard the key points around the factory and make serious representations to the Japanese Consul, demanding severe punishment for the culprits and compensation for the losses. The recent cases in Fuzhou and Guangzhou can serve as precedents. No excuses or evasions should be tolerated. A brief map is attached for your perusal and approval. It is in the public interest. Sincerely, The Shanghai Municipal Government.

Taxpayer Association's Telegram and Letter: The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association sent out two telegrams and one official letter yesterday, as follows: ⑴ Telegram to the Executive Yuan, addressed to President Sun of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing. "At 2:30 AM on the 20th of this month, violent Japanese residents set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company factory and boldly resisted the suppression of the Shanghai First Special District Municipal Council police, killing one police officer and seriously injuring two others. Furthermore, on the same afternoon, they gathered hundreds of people and vandalized shops on North Sichuan Road and Laobazi Road. The entire city is shocked, and the public's outrage is indescribable. We believe that the violent Japanese are planning to create a serious situation in various places to divide our nation's public sentiment. If the central government does not sever diplomatic relations with the violent Japanese or adopt further measures, the people will be helpless and unable to take active measures to cope. We urgently request that you devise a method to dispatch effective police forces to assist the Municipal Council in maintaining security. This urgent telegram is submitted for your consideration. Sincerely, The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association, Ma (seal)." ⑵ Telegram to the Municipal Government, addressed to Mayor Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Government. "Violent Japanese residents set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company factory, killing and injuring multiple police officers of the First Special District Municipal Council. Furthermore, they gathered hundreds of people on North Sichuan Road and Bazi Road and vandalized shops. This serious situation is already clear to you, Mayor. The district has a population of millions, with Chinese people accounting for over 950,000, and our interests are even more closely intertwined. The Municipal Council's police force in the district seems insufficient to maintain security. We specially request that you, Mayor, consider dispatching effective police forces to assist the bureau in maintaining security so that the lives and property of the district's residents can be protected. We anxiously await your response. Sincerely, The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association, Ma (seal)." ⑶ Letter to the Municipal Council. "We are writing to inform you that, according to reports, at 2:30 AM on the 20th of this month, violent Japanese residents set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company factory and boldly resisted the suppression of your bureau's police, killing one police officer and seriously injuring two others. Furthermore, at 3 PM on the same afternoon, they gathered hundreds of people and vandalized shops on North Sichuan Road and Laobazi Road. Our association is filled with indignation. The violent Japanese regime's treatment of the Korean people under its rule, wantonly killing thousands of our country's residents in that area without taking responsibility, has already disqualified it as a modern nation. Starting on September 18th of last year, they deliberately fabricated incidents, violated international covenants, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and used military force to invade key areas of our country's Liaoning and Jilin provinces. Despite Japanese Envoy Yoshizawa's guarantees at international meetings not to expand military operations, they further occupied Heilongjiang, invaded Jinzhou, and eyed Rehe, seized the Beining Railway, and disregarded the interests of other countries. This kind of barbaric and inhumane behavior is even more unacceptable for a modern nation. Perhaps because the matter is in the Northeast, the various foreign residents residing in this district have not witnessed it firsthand and believe that the barbarity of the violent Japanese could not be so extreme. But what about now? Your bureau's police officers are wantonly killed and injured, and the security of the district is wantonly disrupted. Do they still have any regard for the existence of your bureau? Our association believes that your bureau is jointly owned by the residents of the district, and the violent Japanese's insult to your bureau and disruption of security is precisely an insult to the residents of this district and a disruption of their security. How can the residents of this district stand by and do nothing? We originally thought that your bureau must have the ability to maintain security or would not need external assistance. We are corresponding with your bureau to request that you strengthen your police force to maintain security and hope to receive a prompt reply to address the urgent situation."

Statements from Two Organizations: ⑴ Joint Declaration. "The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Citizens' Union issue a joint declaration regarding the violent Japanese residents. It has been verified that violent Japanese residents set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company factory, killing and injuring multiple police officers of the First Special District Municipal Council and vandalizing countless shops on North Sichuan Road and Laobazi Road. This kind of barbaric behavior is a premeditated overall plan by the anti-modern-nation violent Japanese and is not merely an individual problem of the Sanyou Industrial Company, nor is it merely a matter of interests for the shops on North Sichuan Road and Laobazi Road, nor is it merely a question of the Municipal Council's ability to maintain security. It is actually a problem for all of Shanghai and all of China concerning Japan. Currently, the violent Japanese are not only at odds with the Chinese people but also with the foreign residents of all related countries. Under the current circumstances, the Municipal Council is a jointly owned Municipal Council of our country's residents and foreign residents. Now, the violent Japanese residents dare to obstruct the performance of public duties by the police officers of the Municipal Council, who are responsible for maintaining security, killing and injuring multiple people and disrupting security and vandalizing shops. It is as if they view the Municipal Council as something completely insignificant. Our association believes that this kind of behavior is due to our national government not severing diplomatic relations with the violent Japanese, resulting in the inability to exercise the rights of expulsion and sanctions. This should be reported to the government, and diplomatic relations with Japan should be severed immediately, and further measures should be implemented. Otherwise, if we only focus on minor details, we fear that the scope of their barbaric behavior will continue to expand without end. Looking at the case of the destruction of the Sanyou Factory, the Municipal Council seems to have the responsibility to maintain security, but unfortunately, the police force is insufficient and dare not confront their marines. We should devise a method to assist them. This should be requested of the government: that they dispatch effective military police to assist the Municipal Council in maintaining security. As for our residents, they should actively organize and unite and no longer be as disorganized as before, thinking that associations are useless. It must be understood that unity brings strength, while division brings weakness. To confront the violent Japanese residents, all the city's residents should unite. Our associations have been entrusted with great responsibility by the shops and residents, and we dare not lag behind in resisting Japan and saving the country. We especially hope that all the public organizations in Shanghai will unite as one, with the masses united like a fortress. Our association members vow to fight to the death and will not turn back. We issue this declaration for your public consideration. January 21st, Republic of China year 20." ⑵ Telegram to the Executive Yuan, addressed to President Sun of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing. "Yesterday morning at 2:30, violent Japanese residents set fire to the Sanyou Industrial Company factory, killing and injuring multiple police officers of the First Special District Municipal Council. At 3 PM, they vandalized countless shops on North Sichuan Road and Laobazi Road. People in both the commercial and industrial sectors are in danger, and every resident in the city is disheartened. If we do not immediately sever diplomatic relations with the violent Japanese and expel and sanction them, the harm will be even greater than severing diplomatic relations. What will happen later? Now, the violent Japanese have disregarded the police power of the Municipal Council, and its ability to maintain security will be greatly reduced. Shanghai has a total of three million residents, and their property is countless. This hub of Sino-foreign trade and economy should be preserved immediately. We specially request that, in addition to immediately severing diplomatic relations with Japan, effective military police should be dispatched to assist local military police and provide effective protection to ensure the safety of lives and property. We anxiously await your response. Sincerely, The United Federation of Shanghai Commercial Circles and the Shanghai Citizens' Union, Ma (seal)." ⑶ Telegram to the Municipal Government, addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Government. "The violent actions of the Japanese residents are presumably within your government's knowledge, and we will not elaborate further. Now, the violent Japanese are obstructing the exercise of police power by the First Special District Municipal Council and daring to kill and injure police officers. Shanghai's security is, of course, at risk. We specially request that the government consult with the First Special District police authorities to establish a joint defense and maintain security, and request that the government dispatch effective troops for protection. We anxiously await your instructions. Sincerely, The United Federation of Shanghai Commercial Circles and the Shanghai Citizens' Union, Ma (seal)."

Resolutions of the City Federation's Branch Meetings: The Seventeenth and Twenty-Fifth Branches of the Shanghai Special District City and People's Federation held a general membership meeting at the Sichuan Road YMCA at 2 PM yesterday, with over 500 attendees. Li Xingzhi, Wang Ren'e, and Gu Wensheng were elected as the presiding committee. First, Fan Muxian reported on the violent acts of the Japanese ruffians. Discussions then began, and the following resolutions were passed: ⑴ Severely warn the Chinese Concession authorities that they must immediately strengthen their defense forces. ⑵ Each shop should equip itself with警笛警笛 and truncheons for self-defense. ⑶ Each shop should equip itself with pistols and expand the organization of volunteer corps, with each shop having at least one member, and purchase rifles, requesting that the Municipal Council waive the registration requirements. ⑷ A detailed investigation should be conducted into the losses of each shop, and compensation, punishment of the culprits, and apology should be demanded from the Japanese Consul. ⑸ If the goals of compensation, punishment of the culprits, and apology are not achieved, the entire city will not pay the municipal general tax. ⑹ A self-defense corps committee will be organized. ⑺ The Citizens' Union will be requested to convene a city-wide Citizens' Union meeting on a regular basis and actively prepare for it. ⑻ The withdrawal of the Japanese Marine Corps will be demanded. ⑼ Representatives will be sent to meet with Chairman Macnaghten of the Municipal Council. It is also reported that the City Federation's District Branch, the Twenty-Sixth District Branch, the Fifth District Commercial Federation, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Ten-Member Group, and representatives from various national goods factories also held meetings and made statements.

Local News Two

Li Jingcong Discusses the Northwest Trial Flight 97

Preparation Process · · · Trial Flight Situation

This time, Eurasia Aviation Corporation, undeterred by dangers and difficulties, conducted the only long-distance Northwest trial flight in the world, and safely flew back to Shanghai on the 13th of this month. Although newspapers have competed to publish news about this great success, they have all been brief and lacking in detail. The Daily News reporter, recognizing that the Northwest is in the same position as the Northeast, and that the Northeast is already in a critical situation, believes that the Northwest's transportation and all other aspects cannot be ignored any longer. Therefore, yesterday, the reporter visited Mr. Li Jingcong, who led the flight to the Northwest, at the company to make a more detailed inquiry. Mr. Li was kind enough to tell everything he knew. It is disclosed here urgently, which I believe will be welcomed by those who are concerned about national affairs. The following is Mr. Li's account:

Preparation Process: Last autumn, Wang Boqun, the Minister of Transportation, believing that the situation in the interior and remote areas was too isolated and the flow of information was too obstructed, which had too far-reaching effects on national defense, culture, politics, and industry, etc., ordered Eurasia Aviation Corporation to actively prepare for the Northwest route. The company, also believing that this route was being watched by the government and hoped for by the people, and that the Shanghai-Chongqing line was affected by the violent Japanese and could not fly as planned, decided to prepare for the trial flight despite the hardships. In October last year, the two general managers sent me (Li's self-reference) and Schmidt to Beiping to carry out the preparations. The main points of the preparation were: first, the selection of the route. Based on geography and climate, we originally planned to take a route from Shanghai to Beijing, through Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, directly into Xinjiang, completely flying over the hinterland of the commercially prosperous area. Later, due to the prevalence of bandits in Gansu and the inability to transport gasoline, we changed to the current route that has been successfully test-flown, from Shanghai to Beijing, Shandong, through Beiping, Guihua, Ruoshui River, directly into Xinjiang. This route mostly flies over high mountains and ridges, vast deserts and wilderness, with no human habitation and a very bad climate. Second, the transportation and storage of gasoline. Since we had decided to use the desert route, we had to urgently transport and store gasoline at Ruoshui River, the center point 2,600 kilometers long between Beiping and Dihua, so that the plane could refuel midway. Moreover, because it would take at least two months to transport from the interior to Ruoshui River, if we did not do so urgently, it would not be possible to test-fly at the end of December last year. However, inland merchants traveling between the interior and Xinjiang via Ruoshui River only knew how to follow a certain route to cross the river, and were completely unaware of the name of the river crossing location, the surrounding terrain, whether there were any targets that could be used for aerial observation, and landing sites for the aircraft. Therefore, we had to hire a Swedish man, Sheng Ruiheng, at a great cost, who was familiar with the local situation, to transport and store the gasoline for us. Sheng Ruiheng also drew a rough map of the upper reaches of the Ruoshui River, about forty kilometers from the Juyan Sea at the Fork River, which was suitable for aircraft landing and easy to use as an aerial observation target, and handed it to us. The gasoline was stored there. As for the gasoline used in Xinjiang Province, although the Ministry of Transportation telegraphed the Xinjiang Provincial Government to purchase it from Russia on its behalf, it was faster and cheaper than transporting it from the interior. Third, the preparation of equipment. Flying over mountains and ridges, vast deserts and wilderness, with no human habitation, and difficult to rescue, it is the only long-distance desert route in the world, and its equipment should be such that it is not easily damaged, is suitable for long-distance flight, and has considerable proof in the record. The aircraft used by the company at that time was the Junkers W33 all-metal aircraft and the Junkers L5 200-horsepower engine, which were suitable for all these conditions, and were supplemented with various additional equipment. Therefore, it was able to fly about 20,000 [units of distance] back and forth without repair or inspection, and without any failures. As for personnel, in addition to reporting to the Ministry of Transportation and forwarding a telegram to Chairman Jin in Dihua to seek his consent in advance, we also asked the relevant authorities in Suiyuan and Ningxia Provinces to issue a circular to the military police and league banners along the route to assist in protection. In terms of publicity, we also earnestly requested the Ministry of Transportation to consult the relevant agencies to ask them to hand over the official documents sent to Xinjiang to the company to carry with them, and also sent a letter to the General Post Office to ask them to select some of the mail sent from Beijing, Shanghai, Pingjin, and other areas to Xinjiang and hand it over to the company to carry for free. In addition, we also carried free of charge various major newspapers in Shanghai and Pingjin, as well as the Northwest Trial Flight Special Issue printed by the China Weekly and the China Weekly Society. The above is about the outline of the preparation process.

Trial Flight Situation: The Northwest route has been described above, and it takes the route from Shanghai via Nanjing, Jinan, Beiping, Guihua, Ruoshui River, Hami, Dihua, to Weitangzi near Tacheng on the Sino-Russian border. The entire route is divided into three sections of flight: the first section is Shanghai to Beiping, the second section is Beiping to Ruoshui River, and the third section is Ruoshui River to Weitangzi. Each section requires one day's journey. Except for the first section, which is the inevitable route of the company's Shanghai-Manchuria line, there are no high mountains or ridges in terms of geography, there are few sudden changes in terms of climate, there are parallel railways in terms of transportation, and rescue is possible everywhere. Since it was opened last year, there has never been an accident, so it is not necessary to carry out another test flight. However, in order to confirm that the news between Shanghai and Xinjiang can be reached in the shortest time, I led the flight on December 13 last year, carrying mail and news from Shanghai to Xinjiang, such as the Shen Bao, the Xin Wen Bao, the China Weekly, and the Northwest Trial Flight Special Issue printed by the newspaper, and set off north. We passed through Nanjing, because we had to report the trip to the Ministry of Transportation and carry documents from various agencies to the Xinjiang Provincial Government, and stayed for half a day. We continued to fly to Beiping early on the 14th, in order to proceed west on the 15th according to the original plan. Later, we received a telegram from Chairman Jin in Dihua, telling us that the gasoline had not yet arrived, and asking us to postpone the trip. We had to change our plan and take off from Pingjin at 7:00 am on the 20th, carrying mail and news from Pingjin to Xinjiang, and arrived at Guihua at 9:50 am via Zhangjiakou Pingdiquan. We continued to move forward at 11:00 am, passed Baotou, crossed Wolf Mountain, and arrived at Ruoshui River at 4:30 pm. It is estimated that this section (the second section) from Beiping to Wolf Mountain, a part of it follows the Ping-Sui Railway, and a part of it is flying along the old course of the Yellow River. Although the conditions for safe flight are not as good as the Shanghai-Ping section, there are still ways to think of in case of failure. From Wolf Mountain to Ruoshui River in the west, there are about eight or nine hundred [units of distance]. Except for the winding camel road, there are two or three Mongolian yurts and a water well every tens of [units of distance], which are not suitable for straight-line aerial flight, and the rest are high mountains and ridges, towering peaks, vast wilderness, boundless, no water, no grass, and no traces of life. When arriving, there are unpredictable climate changes. Under these circumstances, without extremely skilled technicians and extremely solid aircraft parts, it is easy to happen if one engages in exploration. If something happens, it will not only be difficult to replenish and rescue, but it will also take a lot of time, and it will inevitably become a dried carp. When the plane arrived at the Ruoshui River at 4:30 pm, it immediately searched for the gasoline storage location according to the map drawn by Sheng Ruiheng. However, although there is flat ground in the coastal area, it is interspersed with sand mountains, and Mongolian yurts are mixed in the bushes. In addition to being able to fly over it and look down by chance, it is extremely difficult to find by looking sideways. In addition, there are no other cities, villages, or special buildings that can be used as targets. As a result, the gasoline deposit location could not be found after circling in the air for a while and a half. Moreover, as it was getting late and the weather was getting colder, we had to land in the deserted suburbs of an ancient city about eighty or ninety kilometers from the Juyan Sea that we had discovered. The weather became even colder at night, and the thermometer dropped to thirty-one degrees below zero. We all lay on top of each other in the plane, like sardines placed in a tin can. According to the investigation, the city is Heichengzi, built in the Han Dynasty. Marco Polo used to pass through it twice from Rome to China. Later, it was submerged by sandstorms due to strong climate changes. Now, except for the city walls and streets that can still be clearly distinguished when viewed from the air, the traces of life have long since disappeared. We believe that the fuel in the plane is only enough for one hour of use, and we are deeply afraid that we will not be able to find it if we take off again for three days, and we will be in a difficult situation. Therefore, we fired countless blank shots that night and early the next morning, hoping that someone would come, but we knew that not only did we hear nothing, but we did not even see a bird or beast. After 12:00 on the 21st, we summoned the courage to take off again to search. When approaching Juyan Sea, we happened to encounter a camel herd, and we immediately descended to inquire. We were delighted to learn that the camel herd was Sheng Ruiheng transporting gasoline on behalf of the company, and had only arrived at the Ruoshui River four days ago and put it there to graze. After he indicated the shape and direction of the gasoline storage pool, we took off again. After about ten minutes, we arrived at our destination. A German and two Chinese people from the Sino-Swedish Scientific Expedition Team are stationed in this place, working hard all year round to test the climate, hoping to contribute to the scientific community. At night, we stayed in the Mongolian yurt where the German lived. At 10:00 am on the 22nd, we continued westward, crossed the northern branch of the Tianshan Mountains, passed Hami Turpan, and followed the Tianshan Gorge straight to Tonghua. It was already 5:30 pm. Because the journey was hard and the new land was extremely cold, often thirty degrees below zero at night, we planned to rest for a few days and then conduct a trial flight to Weitangzi on the extreme edge. Later, two fighter planes purchased by the Xinjiang Provincial Government from Russia happened to fly from Weitangzi to Dihua by Russian pilots on the 24th. In addition to inquiring about the details of the journey, as a reference, we also learned that there is only thick fog near a certain mountain between Dihua and Weitangzi every day at noon, but high flying will not touch the mountains. In addition, there were no other unsuitable flying conditions along the way, so we did not go there. It is estimated that this section (the third section), except for the section from Dihua to Weitangzi, which is not very difficult, as described above, the section from Hami to Dihua, because the Turpan lowlands are 200 meters below sea level and extremely hot in summer, making it extremely difficult to navigate, but it is still possible to proceed along the southern foothills of the Tianshan Mountains. In addition, there are no other unsuitable flying conditions. As for the section from Ruohe to Hami, the difficulty is the same as that from Wolf Mountain to Ruoshui River, and flying over the Tianshan branch that runs from north to south is more difficult than flying over Wolf Mountain, because Wolf Mountain is not very high, and the low point of the Tianshan branch is also 2,600 feet. We lived in Dihua for a total of seventeen days, and the people hung flags to welcome us, and the government warmly welcomed us. The Xinjiang Provincial Government and the people deeply hoped that the company's route could be realized as soon as possible, so that Xinjiang's national defense, culture, politics, industry, and so on could all be directly or indirectly benefited. In addition to being busy with social events, we also actively carried out various matters that should be contacted and investigated, such as where the Sino-Russian joint transportation should be, whether the radio can be installed properly, how to set up climate testing, entrust the construction of factory sheds and houses, and the output of valuable goods, and the amount of mail. The various matters were handled properly, and the gasoline arrived at 12:00 on the 7th of the month. We immediately took more than one hundred catties of valuables entrusted by the Xinjiang Provincial Government, as well as many official letters to various agencies in the interior, and 20 kilograms of mail sent from Xinjiang to Pingjin, Beijing, and Shanghai, and rushed to the airport to prepare for the return journey. That night, we stayed in the Mongolian yurt inside the airport. At 9:30 am on the 8th, we took off from Dihua, except for circling Dihua City once to express our gratitude, and then followed the old road to Ruoshui River. We arrived at Ruoshui River at 5:00 pm and stayed in the Mongolian yurt prepared by the Sino-Swedish Scientific Expedition Team. At 7:30 am on the 9th, we left Ruoshui River, passed Guihua at 12:30 pm without stopping, and flew directly to Beiping. We arrived in Beiping at 3:00 pm. We rested for three days, flew to Nanjing on the 12th to report the successful trial flight to the Ministry of Transportation, and flew back to Shanghai on the 12th. It took exactly one month from the departure from Shanghai on December 13 to the return to Shanghai on January 13, which is also a coincidence. (To be continued)

River Pirates Rob and Murder in the Shallow Waters of the Yangtze River 98

The Tragedy Occurred Upstream of Yuezhou

Six Crew Members Killed and Ten Kidnapped

The shallow waters of the Yangtze River have caused significant losses to the operating revenues of the various river steamers on the upper and lower reaches. The shallow waters of Taizi Islet obstructed the steamers on the lower reaches, with as many as seven ships stranded last time. Although the Jianghai Customs Shallow Water Survey Ship has recently discovered a new channel with a draft of fifteen feet, it has just been discovered and has not yet been opened to navigation. In recent days, eight or nine more steamers sailing downstream have been obstructed in the area, using barges to transport and transfer cargo. The various steamers are delayed for a long time, delaying the schedule, and the travelers are suffering. On the upper reaches of the river, the recent shallow waters have also obstructed ships, resulting in robberies by river pirates, and even the tragedies of killing crew members and kidnapping passengers. The details will be recorded as follows:

Meishan Crew Members Killed: Mobil Oil Company has a number of steamers on the Yangtze River that transport kerosene and carry passengers and cargo, traveling to and from Shanghai, Hankou, Yichang, and Chongqing. The company's Meishan steamer was transporting cargo from Yichang this time, and there were no passengers on board. On the 7th of this month, when the ship arrived at the Yangling Islet River surface, a place called Yangling Islet, 25 nautical miles upstream of Yuezhou, it encountered shallow water. The Jianghan Customs had issued an earlier ban, stipulating that all ships traveling on the upper reaches of the river are not allowed to sail at night, in order to prevent accidental grounding on beaches. The Meishan steamer anchored at Yangling Islet, waiting to sail again the next morning. Unexpectedly, the bandits in the area were very fierce, specializing in robbery. They saw the Meishan steamer anchored and a large group of bandits boarded the Meishan steamer in civilian boats, hoping to rob it. It was found that there was no wireless telegraph on the Meishan steamer. When the bandits robbed, the crew had to take their own firearms and fight back with all their strength. The crew was outnumbered and the bandits rushed onto the ship, killing two crew members who resisted on the spot and throwing their bodies into the river. The money and items in the ship were all looted. Temporarily, eight crew members and sailors were kidnapped. According to a telegram received in Shanghai yesterday, four of the eight people kidnapped by the bandits had been killed by the bandits, and the whereabouts of the other four were still unknown. Now the Meishan steamer has been towed down by a ship sent by the company, and the losses from the theft on the ship are very large.

Jiejiang Crew and Passengers Kidnapped: The Shanghai-Chuanhe direct shuttle steamer No. 2 of the Jiejiang Company of this port was loaded with cargo and passengers and sailed to Yichang. On the 15th of this month, when the ship arrived at the felt hat beach, a place called Jinghekou, it was anchored as usual due to shallow water, waiting to sail again the next morning on the 16th. Unexpectedly, just after anchoring, the bandits on the shore knew about it. That night, the bandits led a crowd to board the ship and rob it. Baker, the owner of the ship, was punished by the crew of the Meishan steamer who were brutally killed by the bandits. He was deeply afraid that this bloody tragedy would be staged again, so he adopted a non-resistance policy. Therefore, when the bandits boarded the ship, he allowed the bandits to rob him without resisting. Therefore, although the bandits fired guns to show their power, they did not harm human lives. The bandits' goal was money. In addition to searching for cash and clothing on the ship, it was not enough to satisfy the bandits' desires. Before leaving, they kidnapped the shipowner Bao Zi, two sailors, and three passengers. The kidnapped crew and passengers have been taken to the bandit's den to extort huge sums of money to redeem them. The goods in the ship were not taken away. After the incident, the Jiejiang Company sent the Yichang steamer from Hankou to the felt hat beach to tow the No. 2 steamer to Yichang, and asked the US warship stationed in Hankou to protect it so that no accidents would happen again. Since the robbery of the two American ships, crew members and passengers were killed and kidnapped by bandits, the companies have reported to the American consul, requesting the Hubei authorities to find a way to arrest the bandits and rescue all the captives. It is heard that our country's navy has sent warships to patrol the upper reaches of Yuezhou and protect the merchant ships that come and go.

The Yangtze River Transferred Shallow Water Ships: In recent days, ships sailing on the Yangtze River can only load 20% or 30% of their cargo due to shallow water. If they load more, they cannot pass through. The various ship companies have suffered huge losses. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company specially transferred the Yichang shuttle steamer Kuali back to Shanghai to change to the Shanghai-Hankou route, in order to adjust operations and cope with the difficulty of the Yangtze River's shallow water. The ship will arrive in Shanghai and start sailing immediately.

Resumption of Work at Wusong Yong'an Yarn Factory 99

The Yong'an No. 2 Yarn Factory on Yunzao Road, Wusong, has been closed since the tragic incident on the evening of December 20 last year, for a month now. After the incident, the factory immediately filed a lawsuit in court, and workers Shen Yongming and others were detained one after another and are still on trial. The workers requested the factory to pay four months' bonus, but the factory thought the amount was too large and there was no such precedent, so although the Social Affairs Bureau mediated several times, there was no result. It is learned that the factory, after announcing the closure, felt the plight of the workers, so it completed the organization of the machines and resumed work yesterday. The male and female workers went to work one after another after hearing the news. The order in the factory is still maintained by the police team. It is heard that the objects destroyed by the factory and the losses from the shutdown will cost about more than 300,000 yuan.
