Two Chinese Detectives Extort Money from Suspects 101

After Discovery, Police Station Requests Severe Punishment

Chen A'er, a native of Jiangbei, was carrying smoking paraphernalia on Laodagu Road at 5:00 PM on the 18th of this month when he was stopped by Chinese Detective Yan Enshan, No. 1817, and Chinese Detective Qiao Zhaoyun, No. 1265, of the Xinzha Police Station. They arrested him, and Detective Yan found seventy silver dollars on Chen's person. Yan told Chen that if the money were discovered by the police station, it would be confiscated, so it would be better for him to keep it safe and return it to Chen upon his release from prison. Consequently, the detective deposited the money at a porridge shop at No. 326 Aivenyi Road before taking Chen to the police station. Unexpectedly, Chen reported the incident to the prison warden while in the police station jail. The warden informed the police chief, who considered the two detectives' behavior to be a violation of Article 337 of the criminal law regarding fraudulent acquisition of property. He ordered their detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special Court's criminal division. Detective Qiao hired lawyer Chen Tingrui for his defense. The police station's lawyer, Qian Jiu, argued that since the two defendants, Yan and Qiao, were public officials, they should be severely punished for knowingly breaking the law. Subsequently, Chen A'er, Wang Xiaogou, and Wu Xizi from the Aivenyi Road porridge shop testified, proving that Detective Yan took and deposited the money. However, they could not prove that Qiao Zhaoyun was involved in the conspiracy. Judge Shen Shumu reviewed the evidence and questioned Yan and the others, but they denied the allegations. As a result, the court sentenced Yan Enshan to six months in prison and acquitted Qiao Zhaoyun. Qiao posted bail, ensuring his availability for any further proceedings during the appeal period.

Three Murder Cases 102

A Child's Body with Hands and Feet Bound Found in the Huangpu River: Yesterday, the body of a child was found floating near a buoy at No. 13 Yangshupu. A patrol boat from the Water Police Station retrieved the body. The deceased was only about two years old, with his hands and feet bound by ropes, suggesting he had been murdered and thrown into the river to drown. The body has been taken to the Salvation Bureau, and an investigator has been dispatched to the local court to conduct an autopsy.

A Girl's Body with a Neck Wound Found: Yesterday morning, a small wooden box was discovered in a trash can behind Baolong Lane, Yifeng Lane, inside Ximen. Upon inspection by patrol officers, it was found to contain the body of a girl. The girl was only about two years old, completely naked, with a blood-stained cloth shirt beside her. The child's neck had a knife wound, and her entire body was covered in blood. The Second District, First Precinct, was immediately notified and instructed the local leader, Jin Qiren, to report to the local court for an autopsy.

A Woman's Body with Hands and Feet Bound with Cotton Yarn Found: Yesterday morning, an unidentified female corpse was discovered on vacant land belonging to the Mitsubishi Company in Behetang, Lanlidu, Pudong. The deceased appeared to be in her thirties, wearing a straight gongni cotton-padded jacket and pants. However, her hands and feet were bound with cotton yarn ropes on the outside, and no injuries were found underneath. It is proven that she was murdered before her death, as there is no reason for her limbs to be bound otherwise. The Third District Police Station has instructed the local leader, Xie A'long, from the Twenty-fourth District, to report to the court for an autopsy.

Using Bad Checks to Defraud Goods 103

Geng Desen, Yu Ziqing, Shao Lianzhai, and Dai Xiangsheng jointly opened the Gengda Foreign Goods Store at No. 26 Fadama Road in December of last year. They successively purchased drugs, foreign goods, cosmetics, and other goods from 26 companies, including Jihua Tang Pharmacy, Huazhang Store, Shanghai Factory, Peacock Society, and Guang Shengxiang. They paid with checks from the Longchang Qianzhuang with a due date of the 20th of the same month. When the banks attempted to collect payment from the Qianzhuang on the due date, the checks were returned due to insufficient funds. When the companies tried to collect from the store, it had already closed down on the same date as the check expiration, and the people had fled, taking all the goods with them. Only then did the money houses realize that the store had deliberately engaged in fraud by issuing bad checks. Consequently, Yuan Hesong, manager of Jihua Tang, and the other 26 creditors, jointly retained lawyer Lin Yingqing to file a criminal lawsuit with the Second Special Court, accusing the shareholders of the store of issuing bad checks and seeking civil compensation for the amount of the checks. The court accepted the case, and yesterday, Judge Ma Shounan summoned both parties to court for a hearing. The defendants failed to appear, but the plaintiff's lawyer was present and stated the facts of the case, requesting that the defendants be arrested and punished according to the criminal law and the negotiable instruments law, and that civil compensation be awarded for the amount of the checks, totaling 2,038 taels and 63 silver dollars. Judge Ma declared that the hearing would be postponed until the defendants were arrested and brought to court.

The dedication and enthusiasm of the teachers and students of the school in benefiting the disaster victims and contributing to the well-being of society are truly admirable.

Lawyers with Overdue Fees Take Note 105

Pay Fees Within Three Days of Receiving Notice

The Shanghai Bar Association has a total of seven hundred and several dozen members. According to the regulations approved by the Ministry of Judicial Administration, each member is required to pay a monthly membership fee of two silver dollars. If a member's membership fees are overdue for more than four months, the Bar Association is required to report their dismissal from the association according to the regulations. An investigation reveals that there are over forty members with overdue fees. The association originally intended to proceed according to the regulations, but for the sake of convenience, the executive and supervisory committee held a joint meeting and decided to handle the matter in accordance with the regulations. To further facilitate the process, a final notice was reissued yesterday, urging members to submit their overdue fees to the association within three days of receiving this notice. If they do so, their names will be removed from the list of those to be dismissed. Failure to pay within the deadline will result in the loss of membership status starting from the fourth day.

Shanghai Child Welfare Organizations Welcome Xiong Xiling 106

Decided to Convene a National Child Welfare Conference

The China Child Welfare Association, aiming to connect various child welfare organizations in Shanghai, held a meeting at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday in the Zhongshan Hall of the Young Men's Christian Association, located at No. 20 Museum Road, to welcome Mr. Xiong Xiling. Zhu Qinglan, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Lu Bohong, and dozens of representatives from various child welfare organizations attended. The meeting was chaired by Dr. Luo Yunyan, Vice President of the Child Welfare Association. After delivering a welcoming speech, they invited Xiong Xiling and Zhu Qinglan to give speeches and decided to convene a national child welfare conference. The details of the previous day's meeting are recorded below.

Attendees: Xiong Buling, Zhu Qinglan, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Lu Bohong, Chen Heling, Pan Shilin from the Shanghai Child Welfare and Education Institute, Hu Yuanzhou from the Shanghai First Disaster Relief Shelter, Zhang Xufu from the Shanghai Orphanage, Feng Liutang, Section Chief of the Fourth Section of the Social Bureau, Li Jin, Commissioner of the Hankou Flood Relief, Wang Zhongfu from the Women and Children Relief Association, Huang Xingjie from the Shanghai Nursery, Wang Aitian from the Child Welfare Association, Hua Jingyuan from the Health Clinic, Wu Zhijian from the Leprosy Relief Association, Huang Jibei from the Puyi Vocational Training Center, Fu Ruoyu from the YMCA, and three Western women, among others.

The meeting commenced with the customary procedures. Following the formal opening, Dr. Luo Yunyan, Vice President of the Child Welfare Association, delivered a welcoming speech. He briefly stated that Mr. Xiong has been running the Xiangshan Child Welfare Institute in Beijing for over a decade. His enthusiasm and experience are greatly admired by all. It is a true honor for them to receive his presence and guidance.

Mr. Xiong's Speech: Mr. Xiong expressed five hopes for the child welfare cause: 1. To unify national child welfare organizations, complementing each other's strengths and compensating for each other's weaknesses. 2. To improve China's early childhood education with scientific and new knowledge. 3. To train specialized child welfare professionals, establish nanny schools, and assign them to serve in various regions, dispatching experts to orphanages in various regions for investigation and improvement. 4. To convene a national child welfare conference annually, rotating the location. 5. To conduct a major publicity campaign on the April 4th Children's Day to make the entire nation aware of the importance of child welfare and to encourage donations to support this righteous cause.

Mr. Zhu's Speech: Mr. Zhu Qinglan briefly stated that various child welfare organizations, such as orphanages and nurseries, have been initiated by sages in various regions of China. Their establishment was not easy, and we must maintain and improve them. We must pay close attention to the child welfare cause. Therefore, a child welfare section was established within the Hankou Flood Relief Committee, hoping that specialized child welfare professionals would take charge. He hoped that the Child Welfare Association could take full responsibility, and he would do his best to assist. He also hoped that the Child Welfare Association could initiate a national child welfare conference to be held annually, imitating the methods of the National Medical Association, in order to gather collective wisdom. He would work together with everyone to make it a success.

Closing Remarks by the Chairman: Finally, Ms. Liu Wang Liming presented a plan for providing relief to child beggars in Shanghai, hoping that various child welfare organizations would cooperate. Following this, Chairman Dr. Luo delivered his closing remarks, stating that Mr. Xiong and Mr. Zhu have been promoting the child welfare cause in China for many years. Today, they have honored us with their presence and guidance, and we would like to express our respect and gratitude to the two gentlemen on behalf of the Child Welfare Association and all the children in the country.

Child Welfare Conference: After Dr. Luo delivered his closing remarks, it was decided that the representatives of the various charitable organizations present would initiate the convening of a national child welfare conference and establish the China Child Welfare Association to prepare for everything and set a date for the conference.

Xiong's Daughter Studies in the United States: After the meeting, Mr. Xiong told a reporter from the Xinshi News Agency that, in view of the importance of the child welfare cause, he had sent his daughter, Xiong Zhi, to Columbia University in the United States to specialize in child welfare issues, hoping that she would return to the country and work hard for the child welfare cause in China.

American Ms. Laim's Mission to China 107

Will Explore Qinghai

The Damei Evening News reports that Ms. Laim, an American member of the Royal Geographical Society of Britain, has recently arrived in China, sponsored by the New York Explorers Club, the U.S. Department of Agriculture, and the New York Brooklyn Museum, to explore Qinghai. She arrived in Shanghai with her husband and assistant a few days ago and is currently negotiating with the Nanjing authorities to obtain a passport. Once the formalities are completed, she will depart. There are three possible routes, which are currently under consideration and have not yet been decided: one is to travel from Beijing to Baotou and proceed along the caravan route, another is to travel to Baotou and then proceed westward through Ningxia, and the third is to enter the provinces of Henan and Shanxi via the Pinghan Railway. The purpose of this trip is to collect information on geography and to explore for Ma Qingshan (transliteration). It is said that this mountain is higher than Mount Everest in India, which is known as the highest in the world. If it can be found, it will be measured and photographed by the American Geographical Society. Along the way, they will collect specimens of ethnology and entomology for the New York Brooklyn Museum and the Carnegie Museum in Pittsburgh. They will also investigate various medicinal materials used in Tibet and collect seeds of various plants for the U.S. Department of Agriculture. All newly discovered plants will be photographed. In addition, they will conduct medical research among the Tibetan people for the American Dental Association. The team will carry sound and silent movie cameras to capture the lives and customs of the Tibetan people. The team will also carry a full range of medical equipment and various medicines, staffed by experienced internal and surgical physicians, who will provide medical treatment to the local people in Tibet in order to get close to them and explore their secrets. This trip is planned to last a year in Tibet, and Ms. Laim will accompany them. According to reports, Ms. Laim is thirty-eight years old and has served as a consul in various places since 1912. In recent years, she has traveled extensively throughout China, as well as in Mongolia, Manchuria, Siberia, and other places.

Report on the Four Banks' Issuance Reserve 112

107th Time

The Four Banks' Issuance Reserve is jointly established by the Yanye Bank, Jincheng Bank, Zhongnan Bank, and Dalu Bank to handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. In accordance with the Reserve's issuance regulations, the issuance of banknotes is fully backed by reserves, with a minimum of 60% in cash reserves and a maximum of 40% in guarantee reserves. A public announcement is made weekly, audited by auditors from the four banks and accountants. The 107th public announcement of the Shanghai Reserve on January 16, 21st year, is as follows: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 27,888,252 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 27,888,252 yuan, including cash reserves of 17,029,172 yuan and guarantee reserves of 10,859,080 yuan.

Central Bank Inspection Report 113

114th Time

The 114th inspection report on the issuance reserve of the Central Bank states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the Bank's issuance of convertible notes. The 114th inspection was conducted at the Bank's Issuance Bureau on January 20, 21st year of the Republic of China, and the results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible notes issued: 28,332,884 silver dollars, including 25,645,055 silver dollar notes and 2,687,829 subsidiary currency notes. Total amount of convertible note reserves: 28,332,884 silver dollars, including cash reserves of 22,024,884 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 19,359,229.45 yuan stored in the Bank's Issuance Treasury, 917,574 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 1,748,080.05 yuan stored in peer banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 6,308,000 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Convertible Notes issued: 250,000 yuan. Total amount of Customs Gold Convertible Note reserves: 250,000 yuan. This reserve includes 100,000 U.S. dollars, stored in peer banks in this city, at a fixed rate of 40% to Customs Gold. As per Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 10% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. January 20, 20th year of the Republic of China. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Zhi Fuxun, Supervisors Yu Qiaqing, Bei Songsun, Wang Jingli, Qin Runqing, Hu Mengjia, Tang Shoumin.

The House of a Puxiong District Security Regiment Platoon Leader Robbed 116

One Thief Shot Dead on the Spot

Gang of Thieves Scared Away Without Successfully Robbing

Zhuangjiajing in Puxiong District is a small market town in the district, conveniently located at a strategic point along the Wusong River. The area is remote, without military or police protection, and is only defended by the locally organized Security Regiment. Therefore, robberies are unavoidable every winter. Wang Jusheng, who owns some assets and is moderately wealthy, runs the Gongtonghe Cloth Shop in the area, which is doing well. His son, Wang Yifu, serves as a platoon leader in the Security Regiment. Due to the environment, he is constantly vigilant and always sleeps with a gun after his winter duty. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 20th of this month, thieves coveted and came to rob his house. It was 2:00 AM, and everyone was sound asleep, with no noise. A gang of more than twenty thieves approached from the south along the banks of the Wusong River, loitering outside the door. Wang Yifu, who was sleeping in the front shop, heard the noise in his sleep and woke up. Recognizing the sound of thieves, he grabbed his gun and got up to defend himself. Soon, the thieves used tools to break down the door. Realizing the danger, he fired a shot with his box cannon, but the door remained intact. So he fired several more shots, one of which hit a thief, who fell to the ground. Yifu's father and brother also woke up upon hearing the gunshots and fired the newly prepared regiment's guns into the air. The thieves, knowing they could not succeed, fled. Yifu's father and son, still fearing the thieves were waiting outside, did not dare to open the door. After observing that there was no sound outside, they cautiously opened the door and found a thief lying on the ground, holding a 1,500-foot electric torch. Beside him were an iron bar and two six-inch pistol shell casings. They went to Huacao Town to report to the Sixth District, First Precinct Police Station and reported to the Security Regiment headquarters. The police station found several pawn tickets on the thief, all from the British Concession, proving that the thief did not come from the local area. The chief of the Sixth District, First Precinct, has inspected the situation and reported it to his superiors. The thief's body has been reported by the local leader to the local court for an autopsy. Zhuangjiajing is located at a strategic point, and defense is crucial. It is hoped that the authorities will establish more police stations to ensure public safety.

Postal Workers' Martial Arts Division Regularly Performs 119

The Postal Workers' Martial Arts Division was established in Shanghai several years ago and enjoys a good reputation. Since hiring Mr. Chunting, a renowned martial arts master from Beiping, as an instructor, the division's affairs have become even more developed. The number of members is increasing daily, all of whom can train diligently. The results are remarkable. The division, aware of the public's lack of martial spirit and its demoralized state, and believing that national strength is impossible without it, has specifically scheduled a public performance starting at 2:00 PM on Sunday, the 24th of this month, at the division's training ground in Xiangyuli, Xingjiaqiao Road, North Sichuan Road, to expand publicity for the enjoyment of martial arts. It is said that there will be no admission tickets, and guests are welcome to visit.

Chongxingchang Plumbing and Electrical Appliances Store at No. 809, Beile Road, specializes in domestic Huanmei materials and contracting plumbing and electrical projects. They are known for their excellent, prompt, high-quality, and affordable service, which has always been praised by buyers. The store is commemorating its anniversary. To thank customers for their past patronage, they are holding a grand seven-day sale with extremely low prices. Therefore, the store and its projects have been very crowded lately.

The Shihua Bookstore in Danfeng Road, inside Laoximen, is about to publish The Romance of General Ma Zhanshan, in view of General Ma Zhanshan's solitary defense of Heilongjiang Province and his steadfastness and outstanding qualities as a model for soldiers. Shanghai Guanhai Monthly Renamed Jianbao 123

Guanhai Shishi, a classified compilation monthly, originally aimed to collect national news and provincial reviews in a timely manner and to facilitate preservation. It followed the principle of reporting rather than creating. It has been published for five issues. The sixth issue has now been published, pioneering a format previously unseen in Chinese journalism. Readers have found it convenient. It is reported that the original name was considered too long and inconvenient, and it has been renamed Jianbao (Clippings). The new name is simpler and easier to remember. The sixth issue still uses the original name and adds the new name to indicate the change. The seventh issue and subsequent issues will use the new name exclusively.

Guangshengtang Chinese Pharmacy Holds Price Reduction Today 124

To show appreciation to its customers, the Guangshengtang Chinese Pharmacy, west of the Xiaocaichang in Baxianqiao, is holding a one-day price reduction today. All medicines and tonics will be discounted by 20%, plus an additional 10% off. For the convenience of patients, if they call (84810), a specialist will be sent by bicycle to pick up prescriptions or deliver medicine, without charging for labor. They will also decoct medicine for customers, dividing the decoction into two portions and returning the medicinal residue for comparison, with fair pricing, at five cents per portion.

National Public Opinion Seized and Released 125

The National Public Opinion Society on Qipurao in this city attempted to deliver the thirty-seventh issue of the National Public Opinion Weekly, which it had published, to the General Post Office on North Sichuan Road for mailing on the 16th of this month, but it was seized in its entirety by the Postal Inspection Office. After the society submitted an explanation to the Central Propaganda Department and various military and political organs in the city, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters issued an order to release it yesterday (the 21st). It is reported that due to the difficulties the society encountered, the publication of the thirty-eighth issue of National Public Opinion has been postponed by one week.

Since its establishment in the autumn of the 18th year, the Shanghai Yonghua Paint Co., Ltd. has always used high-quality raw materials, and the paints are produced under the supervision of academic experts. The quality of various products is excellent, no less than imported goods, and the prices are several times lower than those of European and American goods, so its reputation is growing daily. Within two years, it has not only sold well in various cities in the country, but also in distant Nanyang islands and other places. At a time when promoting domestic goods is emphasized, the company is striving for excellence, manufacturing many new and unique products now displayed at the domestic goods sample department of the Shanghai Bank at the intersection of North Sichuan Road, for people from all walks of life to visit.

Readers' Correspondence

Regarding Student Work by Yu Peizhi 130

Save the Nation by Saving Yourself First

Regarding the path that young people should take, this newspaper has published the opinions of Mr. Wang Leyi and Mr. Huang Juemin successively. Mr. Wang quoted Yi Xiasheng's words, "If you want to benefit society, you must forge yourself into a sharp weapon." Mr. Huang's proposition is to "do worldly affairs with a detached spirit." Both of these ideas are very good, and I especially agree with Mr. Wang's quotation of Yi's remarks. Young people are the vitality and lifeline of the country, and the mission they bear is extremely important. How should we cultivate our knowledge and train our bodies so that we can undertake arduous tasks and cope with difficulties? If we only shout slogans with one breath and with passion, post slogans, or even abandon our books all day long, gathering and marching like bees, this will not only fail to help the difficulties of the time, but will also make the most precious time of our youth a futile sacrifice. The gains do not outweigh the losses, which is regrettable. Moreover, there are bound to be one or two unscrupulous elements among them who take the opportunity to act in the name of patriotism and seek the limelight. Their arguments are very激烈, and their behavior inevitably becomes too extreme. As a result, they only cause pain to their relatives and pleasure to their enemies, which is of no benefit to both themselves and the country, and lose the sympathy of society. Is this not young people isolating themselves from the masses? Therefore, Mr. Huang Yanpei published a short article in "Middle School Students," the first sentence of which is "Save the nation by saving yourself first." I think this can be our motto for young people. Now I will record it below. Save the nation by saving yourself first: 1. Everyone should unite and quickly abandon all thoughts of jealousy, suspicion, selfishness, and self-interest. 2. Train your body well. 3. Believe in science and study science. Finally, the last two sentences: All the good things I think are good, start from your own family. All the bad things I think are bad, start from your own family (Ding).

Preparations for the Annual Meeting of the Jiangsu Social Education Federation 131

Xuzhou, 21st - A special dispatch: The fifth annual meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Federation has been decided to be held in Xuzhou. Twenty representatives from eight counties in Xuzhou held a preparatory meeting at the People's Education Center, setting the meeting period from May 1st to 5th, and nominated seven members of the preparatory committee to be responsible for handling matters. Letters have been sent to various counties to solicit exhibits, with agricultural crops as the center. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education sent Yu Qingtang, Zhao Guangtao, and Mai Xu to prepare the Provincial Xuzhou People's Education Center. Yu and Zhao have inspected several sites for the center in Xuzhou and are awaiting a decision from the Department of Education. Currently, Yu and Zhao have left Xuzhou and returned south to plan for the Yi Education of Huai River Workers in Bengbu.

Graduation Thesis to be Based on 20,000 Words 132

The Ministry of Education, based on the request from the Shanxi Provincial Department of Education regarding the lowest standard for graduation thesis, instructed the department: "The request is received. After reviewing the request, the regulations are not specified in the University Regulations, and can be determined independently by each school. However, the average thesis should be based on approximately 20,000 words and should be written in the national language. In addition, the translation of books should be translated into Chinese in detail. Please be informed accordingly."

University Professors Research Methods of Poison Gas Defense in Detail 133

A person named He Enguang previously submitted a letter stating that in order to fight against the violent Japanese, we should be careful to prevent poison gas. The original letter stated that the use of charcoal masks soaked in hexamethylenetetramine solution to defend against poison gas was theoretically flawed and practically incomplete. Because the research on gas masks in recent times has reached a fairly complete field, it is not as simple as the item mask. However, the preparations for the mask and the order for military doctors to study the rescue of poison gas and university professors to study the defense methods, in addition to the military and political department instructing the military doctors to follow the detailed study of various poison gas poisoning treatment and rescue methods, the Ministry of Education has previously notified various universities and related education departments to inform the chemical professors to study in detail various poison gas technical defense methods. Several schools and chemistry professors are currently discussing and conducting considerable experiments.

Zhejiang University Urges Payment of Arrears 134

Due to the Ministry of Education's failure to allocate the 20th year education funds for Zhejiang University, there was once a wave of resignations from faculty and staff. It has now been learned that the school has already ended the first semester of the 20th academic year, and the amount of funds owed is very large, making it difficult to support expenditures. Therefore, it has sent another telegram urging the Ministry of Education to quickly allocate all the fees owed in full to repay the debts. The school's semester examination for the first semester was not held due to the patriotic movement, and the examination will be held in the second semester to determine academic credits. The course programs that were not completed during the suspension period of the first semester are planned to be extended during the summer vacation to make up for the shortfall.

Gui Chongji Resigns as President of National Central University 135

Central Committee member Gui Chongji was previously appointed as the president of National Central University by the order of the Executive Yuan. Gui expressed his unwillingness to take the position due to various reasons. Although the authorities have expressed their intention to retain him, he has decided to resign due to the school's financial difficulties. He sent a telegram to President Sun yesterday requesting his resignation. The original text is as follows: "To Sun Jun, President of the Executive Yuan: Throughout his life, Chongji has vowed to make education his lifelong career. Since returning to the country, he has never lightly left the lecture hall. Recently, he has been determined to get rid of all political restraints and not be involved in them again. He was appointed as the president of National Central University, and how dare he refuse? Considering the decline of academic morals in recent years, cunning people regard education as a stepping stone, opening up the minds of young people to external pursuits, inducing students to advance their careers, and building trenches against each other to compete. They are serving their own personal interests and ruining the country's century-long plan. Therefore, as soon as the new appointment was announced, disputes were immediately seen. Chongji's foolishness does not want to turn his ambition to run schools into students' patriotism and harm the foundation of the country. Therefore, he is determined to resign and let the more capable people take over. He sincerely begs for your understanding. Gui Chongji respectfully bows."

He Zhensheng and Others Request the Dismissal of Xiang, Director of Jinshan Education Bureau 136

A letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Education

He Zhensheng and other Jinshan celebrities in Shanghai yesterday submitted a letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Education. The letter to the provincial government is transcribed below: "We are submitting this letter to request the dismissal and punishment of Xiang Weixian, the director of the Jinshan County Education Bureau, for dereliction of duty and malfeasance. Xiang Weixian, the director of the Jinshan County Education Bureau, is unfamiliar with education, sloppy in his work, and hides and destroys things. We filed a lawsuit against him on December 5th of last year. However, according to the inspection report of the provincial supervisor Cao, the number of schools has decreased by sixteen and the number of school grades has decreased by thirty-two within five years, which is the ironclad evidence that Xiang has destroyed education. This only refers to the quantity. As for the corruption of quality, we will once again report it to you in detail. Last year's high school graduation examination was handled by Shanghai Middle School Experimental Primary School. The original score for passing the examination was 50 points or more. A total of 155 people participated, and only 23 people passed, accounting for only 15% of the total number of candidates. Xiang witnessed the poor results and knew that it was related to his face, so he had to come up with a strange idea and privately lowered the passing standard. All scores above 20 points were granted graduation. Thus, the number of graduates reached 148 people. Whether or not this examination standard has been approved by the Department of Education, it has already been specified in advance, and it should not be freely increased or decreased afterwards. He is usually not responsible for education supervision, allowing students' levels to decline day by day. When there are restrictions during the examination, he arbitrarily lowers the standards to perfunctorily cover up his actions and seek fame and reputation. No wonder that students graduating from our county over the past three or four years have not been admitted to secondary schools in Shanghai. Alas, how unfortunate it is to be a Jinshan student, and how unfortunate it is to be a student under the rule of the current Education Bureau of Jinshan. Who has no hometown, who has no children? The experiences of the students in our county are the same. Those who live in other places cannot help but sympathize with them and think of ways to save them. Xiang Weixian has been the director of the Jinshan Education Bureau for four years. The budget and final accounts have never been announced. It was not until the people repeatedly filed lawsuits that the budgets for the 19th and 20th years were printed and distributed together. However, the order of the items listed in the booklet was reversed, confusing people. For example, the Yi education sub-book for the 20th year is completely different from that of the 19th year. In the 20th year's booklet, the Liugang Elementary School in the 57th section is different before and after the district. Other schools, such as Nanliu Cunyang and other schools, have long been suspended, but the budget is still included. It is clear that the Changong and other schools have owed Changfei for one month each in the 17th, 18th, and 19th years, but they have not been returned in the total expenditures for the 20th year. It seems that the amount owed to the schools, whether it is stored in the bureau or moved for other purposes, is like trying to cover it up. How can he show his integrity and honesty? All of these things are not only known to the whole county, but are also on record. As for the provincial committee members who came to the county to investigate, they were often deceived by Xiang's flattery and good words without realizing it. Today, although the country is in trouble, the provincial government is renewing itself. You take the spirit of rectifying the army and preparing for war, maintain the great plan of planting trees for a hundred years, save the people from water and fire, and help the country in times of danger. In your spare time to manage the country, remember that education is the lifeline of the country. Quickly order the Department of Education to dismiss and punish Xiang Weixian, the director of the Jinshan County Education Bureau, to comply with public opinion and value education. We are anxiously awaiting your orders."

The Middle School Federation Helps Students of Soochow First Middle School 138

A letter to the Shanghai Education Bureau

The Shanghai Middle School Federation, in order to save the country's youth from losing their education, because the entire student body of Soochow First Middle School was unwilling to have the school authorities suppress the anti-Japanese movement and planned to leave the school as a whole, sent a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau yesterday to request permission for the students of Soochow First Middle School to transfer to various schools in Shanghai. The original letter is transcribed as follows: "To the Shanghai Education Bureau: Our association has received a report from representatives of the students of Soochow First Middle School in Suzhou, stating that the students have been severely suppressed by the school authorities for their efforts in the anti-Japanese national salvation movement. The entire student body is eager to save the country and is unwilling to be suppressed. They plan to leave school and transfer to Shanghai as a whole, requesting assistance from our association. Our association sent personnel to investigate and found that the report was true. Yesterday, after careful discussion by the members of our association, it was generally believed that the school was established by the church as a cultural institution for imperialism to invade our country. The government has long had plans to take back the education power. Today, the school dares to blatantly suppress our students' patriotic movement. Our association, based on its purpose of anti-Japanese national salvation, cannot sit idly by when hundreds of patriotic students are suppressed. Therefore, a unanimous resolution was made to pledge full assistance. Your bureau is the administrative organ of Shanghai education. We urge you to order your subordinates to give special preferential treatment to the students of Soochow First Middle School and allow them to freely transfer to various schools. The students of Soochow can achieve their wish to transfer schools and will not be suppressed again. This is not only what our association hopes for, but also related to the dignity of the Chinese nation. We have always admired your bureau's sympathy for students' national salvation movement, and we believe that you will be happy to support us. We are writing specifically to request this, and we hope that you will reply to us. Sincerely, Shanghai Education Bureau."

The Problem of Student Transfers for Mingqiang and Yanmo Students 139

Six Measures to be Formulated and Implemented Immediately

The students of Mingqiang Middle School and Yanmo Girls' School in this city, who have reported losing their education since the school authorities announced the suspension of the two schools, held a meeting of all students at Hualong Road at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the issue of transfers. A total of 59 students attended. Chairman: Tang Yiyu. Recorder: Gan Lijun. They immediately discussed the transfer measures and resolved six proposals: 1. The Executive Committee is responsible for representing the students to the Municipal Education Bureau to request assistance. 2. The association will submit a list to the Municipal Education Bureau, requesting the introduction of reliable schools. 3. The Municipal Education Bureau must reply within three days. 4. Request the board of directors of Qiang and Yan to compensate all students for one year's tuition fees per student. 5. The student's transcript will be inquired by the Executive Committee to the school authorities. 6. Notify all students to come to the Executive Committee for registration, otherwise they will be disqualified and lose the right to transfer schools. The above will be decided at the next general meeting for implementation.

Public Library Improvement Plan of the Public Works Bureau 143

The Public Library of the Public Works Bureau has recently undergone significant improvements, and several new plans will be implemented. In recent days, the number of fee-paying patrons has increased considerably, so the Library Committee has recommended increasing funding to allow more people to read. The annual fee for military personnel will be reduced by five yuan. Qualified school students, with proof from their principal and a guarantee from a taxpayer, will also enjoy this reduced fee, but the books they borrow may not be novels.

The budget for purchasing new books in 1932 has been increased from 1,500 taels to 1,800 taels, and the binding fee has been increased from 500 taels to 600 taels. The budget for newspapers and magazines remains at 1,100 taels, but several Chinese newspapers and magazines will be added this year. Hard covers will be added to all magazines on display. Paper bags and slips will be added to books for loan to prevent damage during transport within the library. Additionally, 50 taels of silver will be allocated to purchase a V-shaped bookshelf transport cart. Regarding the book purchasing policy, the committee advocates that the ratio of fiction to non-fiction books should be three to one.

New Developments in the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Night School 144

Adding Morning Classes and Expanding Subjects

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Commercial Night School has been operating arduously for ten years. Last autumn, recognizing the urgent need for Chinese typing personnel, it established a Chinese typing class. The first session concluded on the 15th of this month, and registration for the second session has already begun. However, the school has found that the number of night school students applying for admission is overwhelming, often exceeding the quota. Due to the limited number of classrooms, many aspiring young students are turned away. Therefore, Principal Lu Fengzhu recently drafted a plan to expand morning classes to accommodate students who exceed the night class quota. This plan was endorsed by Chairman Wang Xiaozai, Standing Committee member Fang Jiaobo, and others. It was decided to greatly expand the morning classes, transforming the Chinese typing class into a clerical studies department and adding a commercial studies department as a remedial option for students exceeding the night class quota. It is reported that the clerical studies department will include three courses: Chinese typing, French, and drawing (library science can be taken as an elective). The commercial studies department will include five courses: commercial knowledge, English, abacus, bookkeeping, and accounting, which are largely the same as the night school courses. This is truly good news for out-of-school youth in the industry. Registration begins immediately. Anyone with a secondary education level or equivalent can enroll. Classes are held every morning from 6:45 AM to 8:30 AM (the practical time for Chinese typing and library science is not included in this). The quota for the clerical studies department is tentatively set at 50 students, and the quota for the commercial studies department is tentatively set at 80 students. Both men and women are accepted. Detailed regulations are available, and a reply will be sent with a one-cent stamp attached.

"Japanese Bandits Under the Microscope" Published 145

Since the invasion of the Japanese bandits, there have been many books studying Japan, but few have been able to fully expose the hideous faces of the Japanese bandits from all aspects. Recently, the World Magazine Agency, recognizing this, specially commissioned a person who has studied Japan for many years and is an expert in Japanese affairs to conduct detailed research on economics, culture, military preparations, politics, and the invasion of Northeast China and Mongolia, compiling all statistics, and exposing the current situation in Taiwan under Japanese imperialism, striving to place the entire Japanese bandit under a microscope so that Chinese people can understand the true face of the Japanese bandit after reading this book. The book is titled "Japanese Bandits Under the Microscope" and contains a total of nineteen articles, such as Xu Gongyi's "Japan's Economic Aggression Policy Against China," Xu Yiqiao's "The Manchurian Problem," Yan Shixiong's "Anatomy of the South Manchuria Railway," and Liu Jiaxun's "Political Organization," with the Tanaka Memorial attached. The entire book contains more than 200,000 words and is priced at six dimes. It can be purchased from the World Bookstores in Shanghai and other provinces.

Strength of Each Team in A Group 147

Tongji: The Tongji University basketball team has always had considerable achievements. According to the team's instructor Li Jiyuan, the strength this season is better than last year. Ji Yubiao and Li Silin have made great progress in their skills, and the remaining players are also considered average. They will surely have a good performance in the future.

Free Talk

Right and Wrong (Below) 153

The current power is the power that takes advantage. In the dictionary of those who bow down to the current power, there is no "right and wrong." If there is, it is annotated differently.

Only allowing oneself to be right and forcing others to be wrong is a common trick of the current power. Sometimes even crying for injustice is not allowed. In this situation, those who suffer injustice can only fight for right and wrong. It is so uneconomical to have to fight for right and wrong with force!

The judgment of right and wrong mostly contains the characteristics of the times, region, and class. One era has its era's "right and wrong," one region has its region's "right and wrong," and one class has its class's "right and wrong."

Using a ruler to measure cloth, using a dipper to measure rice, what are the ruler and dipper for measuring right and wrong? As a member of the modern Chinese masses, I propose the following standards for right and wrong:

(1) What is public is right: What is not public is wrong. What increases the welfare of the masses is right; what harms the welfare of the masses is wrong. When the welfare of the masses conflicts with the welfare of small groups, supporting the welfare of the masses is right; supporting the welfare of small groups is wrong.

(2) What is true is right: What is not true is wrong.

(3) What promotes the progress of the times is right; what hinders the progress of the times is wrong.

Shouzhou Sun Yu Biography Wang Chang 154

Sun Yu was a native of Shouzhou. He was known in his village for his boxing skills. There was a stone in his village that weighed eight hundred pounds. He could carry it for a hundred steps without resting. People called him Sun Eight Hundred. Yu also had high expectations for himself. Wu Qing, the Central Envoy of the Countryside, heard of him and promoted him to Chiliarch. When the Sino-Japanese War broke out in the Guangxu Jiawu year, the Central Envoy volunteered to go out of the pass. Yu was overjoyed and eager to go. He led his disciples of a hundred people and followed the Central Envoy. The scholar's word was big. In fact, he was not familiar with military affairs. He collapsed first upon hearing the sound of cannons and lost his whereabouts. Yu stamped his feet and wept, saying, "How can I face entering the pass now?" He alone led his disciples to trace him. Unexpectedly, they encountered Japanese soldiers. The Japanese army was nearly a thousand strong. Yu measured the situation and was no match for them. He retreated into the forest and had his disciples abandon their horses and climb trees, watching in the dark. The Japanese were unpredictable. They surrounded the forest with troops and searched it extensively. Anyone who entered the forest died. The Japanese were blocked by the forest. Guns could not be used. After a long time, the Japanese also remained silent. Yu and his disciples discussed, saying, "The Japanese are not advancing because they know that fighting in the forest is unfavorable. If they don't leave, will they wait for the cannons to arrive? If the cannons arrive, we will have no chance. It is better to break through quickly. We may still live." So they searched for horses and jumped out in succession. The Japanese were unprepared. They engaged in close combat in a hurry. Yu's disciples fought bravely with waist knives. The Japanese army was forced back. Yu estimated that if they went a little further, they would be trapped by firearms. He and his disciples struggled to disturb them. Enemies and friends were mixed up. They fought and seized each other. The Japanese guns could not be fired in the end. A certain Japanese major was skilled in jujutsu. He jumped from his horse to face Yu. Yu glared and shouted loudly, waving his knife and chopping horizontally. Both the man and the horse were cut in half. At dusk, he had cut down nearly a hundred people by hand. General Zhang Gaoyuan's troops arrived, and they were able to escape. They lost twelve disciples and killed hundreds of Japanese. The Japanese army's morale was shaken. However, due to the defeat of the Central Envoy, the merit was not recorded. He eventually returned to his village as a commoner and lived to old age.

Wang Chang said, "Mr. Weng Yinruo told my late father that Yu was tall and had long arms. He was simple and spoke little. People didn't think much of him. I didn't expect him to be able to kill bandits. Alas! If Yu could find his lord and assist him, how could his merit be measured? However, he was eventually submerged, impoverished, and died of old age. It is sad. However, Yu was still able to kill bandits at that time. Now there are people with Yu's talent, but they are suppressed by incompetent lords, concealing their weapons and dragging their soldiers, rotting their hearts and gnashing their teeth, watching the rampant bandits rampaging and waiting to die. That is even more sad. Alas!"

A Record of the Sino-Western Football Circle Social 155

Jiang Huaiqing

The Malayan Overseas Chinese football team came to Shanghai again. They stayed for ten days and played five games. Although the results were poor, their spirit was commendable. The other night, the Chinese National Sports Association hosted a banquet for the team at Guyixuan on Sanma Road. Leading figures from the Chinese and Western football circles, as well as the Shanghai Port International Football Team of the Westerners Football Association, the Chinese Football Team, and reporters from various newspapers, were invited to accompany them. There were an estimated seventy or eighty Chinese and Western guests, an unprecedented occasion for an ordinary banquet. Therefore, I record the anecdotes as follows.

Eating Guidance: The wine and dishes that night were all Chinese-style. However, there were more than twenty Westerners attending. It has become commonplace for Chinese people to eat Western food. However, it is rare to see Westerners eating Chinese food. Those who have lived in Shanghai for a long time are not short of experts in this regard. However, that night, the players of the port team, British army players such as Lincoln and Scott, the health team, and the special service team were like virgins who had never tried Chinese food. Therefore, they panicked upon arrival and didn't know how to start. This kind of timid and weak state was very different from the mighty demeanor they showed on the football field in front of thousands of spectators. The Sports Association staff Zhou Jiaqi specially instructed Lu Zhongen, Yu Hengzhi, and Chen Zhenhe to accompany them and serve as temporary eating guides. It was truly an interesting event.

Toasting and Singing: In Western customs, there is a ritual of toasting and singing to celebrate each other at banquets. That night, the Chinese and Westerners were mixed, so this kind of etiquette was inevitable. After the chairman Zhao Jinqing (director of the Sports Association) finished his speech, he presented a silver cup to the Malayan Chinese football team, with the four words "Courageous and Diligent" inscribed on it. It was received by the leader of the Malayan team, Mr. Yu Zhuohua. Everyone raised their glasses and sang to congratulate Malaya. After that, the Secretary-General of the Sports Association, Mr. Shen Silang, also expressed his sincere gratitude to the Western Football Association, the press, and the referees for their cooperation and support. The President of the Western Football Association, Green Shaw, and the representative of the British Army Football Team in Shanghai, Cody Hwa, also expressed their warm congratulations to the National Sports Association, the Malayan Football Team, and the Chinese Football Team.

Wishing Success: The Westerner Li Silian has a history of twenty years of overseas Chinese in Shanghai. He knows football very well. Therefore, he is the most experienced and has the deepest knowledge. He has a good impression of the Chinese football circle. He is now the honorary instructor of both the Jinan and Donghua football teams. He was very happy to talk and laugh at the meeting and said that if Jinan wins the Group A championship of the Western Football Association, Donghua wins the Senior Cup and the Scott Cup championship, and China wins the International Football Championship, it will be the supreme glory of your country's football circle. At the time of the speech, he seemed to have infinite hope. Judging from the current situation, Mr. Li's words are not impossible. I hope the athletes will work hard and drink the Yellow Dragon, so as not to live up to the enthusiastic celebration of that night.

They don't approve of party rule, and they don't approve of Puyi being emperor. They say, "There is another true son of heaven somewhere."

Reading Painting Notes · Swallow 157

The collaborative painting exhibition of the Three Friends of Winter, which has been brewing for a long time, was initiated by famous painters Zhang Shanzi, Wang Zhongshan, He Tianjian, Shang Shengbo, Zheng Wuchang, Xiong Songquan, Wang Shizi, Qian Shoutie, Ma Wanli, and Sun Xueni. Those who were invited to join include Shen Jianzhi, Zhu Shaoyue, Hong Shuan, Wang Ziyuan, Xu Xiaocun, and Wu Yifeng. Xue Baolun was elected to preside over the association's affairs. The exhibition was held in Room 311 on the third floor of New World. Every afternoon, landscape, flowers, birds, insects, figures, and animals were painted collaboratively. The period lasted only one week, and more than 170 fine works have already been painted. It is scheduled to be displayed in the left hall of New World on the 22nd, 23rd, and 24th. The reporter followed up on the news and recorded what he saw and heard in the following.

Among the works, flowers, fruits, and animals are the most numerous, followed by landscapes and figures. They are all crystallization products of the painters. Xiong Songquan's giant lion was complemented by He Tianjian's mountain trees. The workmanship is equally matched. Fine landscape paintings include He Tianjian's imitation of Dong Ju, Zheng Wuchang's imitation of the Song and Yuan Dynasties, Shen Jianzhi's study of Wen Tang, Sun Xueni's imitation of Shu Mei, Wang Zhongshan's imitation of Ma Yuan, Qian Shoutie's imitation of Da Chi, and Xu Xiaocun's study of Dai Xi. They all have unique features.

Flowers, birds, vegetables, and fruits, such as Shang Shengbo, Wang Shizi, Ma Wanli, Hong Shuan, Ye Weixin, etc., are all lifelike and fragrant, and are highly regarded in the art world.

Among those who paint animals in Shanghai, Zhang Tiger and Xiong Lion are highly recommended. Those who get their works of art cherish them like treasures. Little do they know that Xiong is proficient in all kinds of animals. Yesterday, I saw the white ape painted by Xiong, complemented by Xue Ni's red trees and Wanli's yellow wisteria and bees. It was extremely exquisite. So I jokingly inscribed it: Dreaming of becoming a marquis is a delusion. After offering the heavenly book, I turned to think. Why not pick the fruits on the branches? I want to send the autumn red to someone. Then I asked Shen Jianzhi to write it. Shanzi and Tianjian collaborated on Rouge Tiger, which is the most precious and not easy to obtain at ordinary times.

On the sixth day, the master of the poetry circle, Xie Yucen, came to visit. Seeing the painting of Fanzhou Tu painted by Xue Ni, he wrote a poem: Carrying wine, the river tide is wide with drunk eyes. The snow-covered reeds connect to the cold sky. If the rainbow is asked about the past, there may be two ordinary girls playing the flute. The words are very similar to Yang Tieya's. It is indeed a good work.

He Tianjian is famous for his landscape paintings. The benevolent daughter never easily puts her pen to paper. However, whenever she feels inspired, she paints a jade face with hanging temples, which is not inferior to Yuhu Danxu, and is even more beautiful and elegant. The painted lady is extremely beautiful in appearance and extraordinary in charm. Wanli filled in a pear tree for it, and I asked him to fill in a small order. I then wrote it as if in a dream: The courtyard is slightly cold and windy, reporting that the pear blossoms are in bloom. With low temples, I think carefully, with thousands of sorrows lingering. Who expected? Who expected? The news is now finally gone.

Wang Shizi is famous for his flower, bird, insect, and fish paintings. The night before yesterday, when I saw Wu Yifeng coming, I suddenly became interested, so I cooperated with Wu to paint a landscape painting. Wang painted the pine trees and hillsides, and Wu filled in the distant mountains. It was just like seamless, and I wrote a poem: The sky is full of clouds pressing down on the mountains, and thousands of peaks and valleys look lost. When the wind is calm and the sun is setting, the sound of the pines is quiet. Someone is walking westward over the bridge with a stick.

Others, such as the New Year's painting, He Tianjian's pine, Qian Shoutie's plum, and Shang Shengbo's peony, are all precious works. It is rare to cooperate at ordinary times. It is said that there are five or six frames, which can be said to be a grand event.

Mr. Wang Changjian. Please indicate the address so that you may receive a valuable contribution. Editorial Department of Free Talk,

Acknowledgments: The famous painter Zhu Wenhou is good at flowers, birds, and beasts. He is especially good at painting monkeys. I am grateful for his gift of a fan page, which is exquisitely unique. I hereby express my gratitude.

Northern Tour Images and Others (3) Yao Sufeng 158

A Self-Description by Movie Star Hu Die:

A Story: While still producing White Cloud Tower, Mr. Hong Shen introduced two actresses. They all had very sincere intentions, strong interest, and a physique suitable for the film industry, as well as other qualities. Mr. Hong meant for them to first visit our actual work to understand some of the work's procedures and methods. Then they could formally begin their own work. They all happily agreed. The first day, the time our shooting work started was at 7 p.m. But before 5 p.m., they had already arrived, waiting without disappointment for those free two hours to pass. They carefully watched me do my makeup, and carefully watched me following Mr. Director's orders, doing this, doing that. The lights were so strong that my eyes felt pricked. The acting was trivial and demanding in a way that annoyed people. The camera made a hypnotic, detestable sound. Everything about the working people—their smiles and actions—had no freedom. This puppet show was much more difficult to stage. At the very least, in the minds of those two, this is how they began to feel. Otherwise, why would they have excused themselves to leave in a hurry because of the lateness of the hour when our work hadn't finished? From tomorrow on, and until now, they haven't paid us another visit. According to Mr. Hong: "They're chickens who know how to do a hundred somersaults!" The stimulation of the story mentioned above isn't my ridicule toward others. It's my stimulation of myself. Although I was an ordinary actor then, I often heard Mr. Zhang Shichuan giving us instruction. He said, "The Chinese film profession is so chaotic. Although there have been some bright sprouts in the past seven or eight years, they are often attacked by a certain kind of dark force. Since we have determined our upward goal, we must work hard to build a solid foundation for the film industry. Speaking of hard work, it's not to say that one person works hard. Everyone must work hard. Everyone must not be afraid of sacrifice. Even if we ourselves can't achieve success, the road to success can eventually allow later generations to find the images we left behind." Therefore, several times I felt discouraged because I felt trapped, and several times I learned to be disappointed because of the unfortunate criticism in society. But in the end, I can muster up our spirits to look forward to future success.

A Record of Cheng Ma's Double Building (17) by the Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio 159

Third Episode: Yu and Liang Arrive Together, Causing the Feast to Dissolve; Yin the Minister Avoids Them, But Who Abandoned the Jeweled Box? (17)

Hearing that someone named Li was calling, An Yutian hurriedly and unsteadily walked out, abruptly leaving behind Liang Xiaoyun, his close friend at the table, without even saying goodbye. He quickened his pace and rushed to the telephone in the office. He saw an earpiece taken off the phone and hung on a small nail nearby, so he took it, put it to his ear, and spoke into the mouthpiece, asking, "Where are you calling from? Is this Normal University? Are you Miss Li?" He then heard a very clear voice from the earpiece saying, "Yes, this is Wenxia. Is this Yutian?" An Yutian quickly replied, "This is Yutian. Oh, Wenxia, I haven't seen you for days. How are you? I'm sorry, I was busy and didn't have time to visit you. I appreciate you calling first." After saying this, his heart started pounding, as if his words were insincere and he felt guilty for lying. Li Wenxia then answered on the phone, "I already know a little about your situation. Teacher Wei, Wei Zhuomou, just told me. I was very shocked, so I quickly called to ask you what exactly happened. How could such an unfortunate tragedy occur in your home?" Upon hearing this, An Yutian secretly marveled. This Mr. Wei really had nothing better to do than deliver messages for me everywhere. It wasn't enough that he brought Liang Xiaoyun, but he immediately went to disturb Miss Li. Fortunately, Miss Li wasn't as impatient as Liang Xiaoyun and didn't come straight to my apartment, which was my good luck. So, he solemnly replied, "That's how it is. But I can't say the details and the solutions for now. I must wait for my uncle An Dakui's second letter. Thank you for your concern. I'm very grateful. But I'm in a state of chaos and feel very weak because of this sudden disaster. Let me rest for a while, and I will visit you there tomorrow to discuss it in detail." He didn't expect that these words wouldn't work as an excuse. Instead, Li Wenxia's voice on the phone became even higher and crisper, saying, "No, I'm worried. I want to see you right away. Wait for me, I'm hiring a car now. We'll talk when we meet later!" Then, with a snap, the earpiece was hung up, leaving An Yutian no chance to speak or stop her. The line was cut. Helpless, he stood there blankly, holding the earpiece, dazed for a while. Suddenly, he remembered that Li Wenxia would come as soon as she said she would. From the dormitory of the Normal University to here, even in the slowest rickshaw, would only take at most half an hour.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Fluctuate Greatly 160

Excess Cash... Shorts Can Enter

Quiet Long Enough to Want Movement, Rebound Weak by Four Tael

Yesterday, the gold price showed great volatility and a chaotic situation. The rise and fall were irregular, with a total difference of thirteen taels throughout the day. Dealers were at a loss and unsure of their positions. The market was strange and unpredictable, truly a case of being quiet long enough to want movement, with a final rebound of about four taels.

The market opened high, rising immediately, probably because a large order unexpectedly fell back. Although the silver price remained unchanged, it did not prevent the market from breaking through six hundred and ninety taels. As foreign exchange tightened initially and then loosened, coupled with major players and long positions vying to sell, and the trend of declining cash, the market sentiment suddenly turned weak, plummeting ten taels and breaking eighty taels. In the afternoon, news of debt defaults emerged, triggering a selling spree, almost a complete collapse, breaking eighty taels again. Subsequently, a deficit in foreign exchange bills led to a rebound. Zhifeng Yong and speculator Wu, etc., rushed to buy, and shorts rushed to cover, resulting in an extremely sharp market with a rapid rise of more than ten taels, suddenly breaking ninety taels. The surge was unstoppable, likely due to short positions being taken advantage of, caused by excess cash, so the exchange's registered prices for all months have become uniform.

Opened High, Plunged Before Noon Closing

Opened five taels higher at six hundred and eighty-nine taels. A large order suddenly decreased by one-eighth. The silver price remained the same, but private telegrams rose by one-sixteenth, which did not affect the market. Subsequently, Wanxing, Tong Taichang, Shunli, and others sold, dropping from six hundred and ninety taels to eighty-seven and a half. Suddenly, buyers became enthusiastic, such as Yuanheng, Hengyu, Yuan Maoyong, Benshichangxiang, Dadecheng, etc., all entering. The initial price of British gold was one shilling ten pence six two five, later five six two five, a jump of four taels to six hundred and ninety-one taels nine qian. Soon after, Yuanmao, Tong Taichang, Hengxing, Chunyuanyong, Shunmao, Yuhe, etc., came to sell, retreating three taels. The opening price of British gold remained unchanged, around six hundred and eighty-nine taels. The internal盘 price of US dollars was one shilling ten pence six two five, followed by a head of one tael or so, from six hundred and eighty-eight taels eight qian to nine taels eight qian. After nine thirty, the foreign exchange market eased, especially with a drop in red notes by only five and a half taels, with few buyers. The selling frenzy on the trading floor, Qian Changxiang, Yuan Chun, Biaofengcheng, Shun Maoyongfeng, Heng Xingyuan, Heng Changyong, Datong, and other banks, were mostly selling off. The bank's buying price for US dollars was thirty-three yuan, and for British gold, one shilling ten pence six two five, resulting in a sudden drop in gold prices, plummeting ten taels until eleven o'clock to six hundred and seventy-nine taels eight qian. Subsequently, Hengxing, Yuanchun, Yuankangxiang, Tong Taichang, Chengdayong, Tongchun, Jinfengyong, Yuandayong, etc., all reduced their positions. Heng Xingyuan also returned to buy. As the US dollar banks absorbed at thirty-two yuan eight seven five, the market suddenly rose, reaching six hundred and eighty-four taels five qian at eleven fifty. It then decreased slightly, about one or two taels, until noon closing at six hundred and eighty-three taels five qian, and was re-priced at four and a half taels, with a listing price still at seven hundred and fifty taels, with a pressure of sixty to seventy taels. Noon closing was sixty-five to sixty-six taels.

Post-Market Change is Endless, Intriguing

The post-market opened at eighty-four taels two qian, then at five taels two qian, immediately returning to two taels eight qian, and at two ten to four taels two qian. However, various firms had little activity. Around two thirty, a storm suddenly arose, due to rumors of Germany defaulting on war debts and reparations, fearing unexpected actions, causing panic. Fuxingyong, Xiexingyong, Yuan Maoyong, Yuhe, Hong Kangyong, etc., all sold, selling US dollars to banks, calculated at thirty-three yuan, and British gold at one shilling ten pence seven five, causing the gold price to plummet more than five taels, reaching seventy-eight taels five qian at three o'clock. Afterwards, the situation seemed to ease. Zhifengyong, etc., bought, adding more than three taels, to eighty-two taels, and then one tael again, until three thirty, when Zhifengyong, Xiexingyong, Yuhe, Dadecheng, Qian Changxiang, and even those who had sold, urgently rushed to buy back. Examining the reasons for the sudden rise, it was due to the improvement in foreign exchange bills. Banks absorbed one-month British gold at one shilling ten pence seven five, forward six eight seven five, and US dollars could be settled at thirty-two yuan six two five to five six two five. Fuchang, etc., all stopped selling and switched to buying, which stimulated the market. The gold price soared eleven taels, and Wu worked hard to push it, reaching six hundred and ninety-two taels at four twenty, exceeding the highest price of the early market, truly an unimaginable change. However, Yuan Maoyong, Qian Changxiang, etc., took this opportunity to sell, causing the price to fall sharply by more than three taels, retreating to six hundred and eighty-eight taels five qian, immediately adding one and a half taels, until the market closed at four thirty at eighty-eight taels eight qian, up three taels eight qian from the previous day, a small reversal of the previous two days. The highest of the day was ninety-two taels, the lowest seventy-eight taels five qian, a difference of thirteen taels five qian. The goods market opened at eighty-nine taels in the early market, noon closing at four taels five, afternoon at four taels five, and closing at eight taels half. The quoted price was approximately seventy taels to sixty taels. Registered accounts for January, February, and March were the same at six hundred and eighty-four taels, afternoon at eighty-nine taels, water subsidy at six hundred and eighty-four taels, afternoon at eighty-nine taels. Red notes increased by only five taels five qian, with buyers hesitating. Only spot firms traded among themselves at seventy taels.

Extremely Complex Over-the-Counter Transactions
