Shen Bao Local Supplement

January 22, 1932 (No Additional Charge)

Small Forum

The Fortunate Riot of Japanese Ronin 177

Since the incident in the eastern provinces, the Japanese have repeatedly attempted to riot in Shanghai. Finally, it suddenly broke out the other day. The Sanyou Industrial Society towel factory in Yinxiang Port was destroyed, and the doors and windows of shops on North Sichuan Road were smashed. Chinese police were killed, and pedestrians were beaten. Such acts of murder and arson were openly committed within our country's territory. Moreover, after the arson, they even convened a meeting of residents to resolve to request the government to earnestly protect the lives and property of residents and the legitimate rights of Japan, and to request the Japanese naval landing force to be responsible for prevention. In our country, people are allowed to run rampant, and the country has not yet perished. The lives of citizens are not guaranteed at all. We want to ask where our government has gone. Where have our 450 million citizens gone!

If the Japanese kill and burn, China can only watch them kill and burn and resign ourselves to fate. From Korea to Tianjin to Qingdao, they kill and burn everywhere and riot everywhere, echoing the brutal army in the northeast. Now they have killed and burned in Shanghai. In the future, they will advance to Nanjing and every city, and tragic scenes of killing and burning can occur anytime and anywhere. Countrymen, touch your heads, do you have any guarantee? Will you still be calm? Will you still wait for death? Do you still think that the fall of the Northeast has nothing to do with you?

The disaster in the Northeast has been going on for more than four months, and the government only tells us to endure and only tells us to wait for death. It neither fights, defends, nor makes peace. It bows to the spirit tablet of the League of Nations every day to beg for help. From the Tianjin riot, the Fuzhou incident, the Qingdao incident, to the current tragedy in Shanghai, the government can only watch with its eyes open, at most issue a "protest" as usual. What is the use of such a mediocre and incompetent government?

Recently, in the memorial draft that Honjo Shigeru presented to the Japanese Emperor, it was said: "The Chinese government has long become a non-responsive, incomplete political system. Although Chiang Kai-shek is very clever, his national thinking is still unsound. The so-called northward recovery of lost territory is nothing but stinking propaganda and has no effect. As for Wang Jingwei and Hu Hanmin, they all have no real strength and no national concept. Zhang Xueliang, with his fine wine and women, is even less worthy of mention... In short, the Chinese government is really not worth worrying about." How bold and cold and venomous these words are! Government officials, listen to them!

The government is so incompetent and irresponsible, so resisting violence and defending against insult, saving the country and saving ourselves, all depends on us rising up to take action, organizing our own armed forces, thoroughly rejecting Japanese goods, and the people themselves announcing the severance of diplomatic relations with the Japanese, with the determination to die for the survival of the nation. Only in this way can we save the country and save ourselves. Nationalists with blood, rise up!

Popular Literature and Art

Respectfully Presented to the Rich by Ze Pu 178

The article "Rich People, Please Turn Back!" by Uncle Ming in yesterday's supplement touched my poetic impulse, and I actually composed several short poems. But there is one statement, please don't misunderstand the rich, it's not that I, a poor man, intend to joke with the rich, but just offer a small opinion, with absolutely no other malicious intentions, know me and blame me, it's all up to you, I'll write this poem below:

(1)

Behind vermilion gates, meat rots,

On the road, bones freeze to death!

The gap between rich and poor is so vast,

Who says it's all the same?

Raise the banner of revolution,

The rich tremble!

The rich tremble,

And still dare to be stubborn?

(2)

Ragged cloth and rotten cotton,

Wrap the body tightly.

Ignite the fire of life,

Burning straight at the rich!

Nowhere to go,

Where can the rich escape?

Where can the rich escape,

Quickly handcuff and shackle them!

(3)

Why are the rich so rich?

Their hearts are worse than dogs!

Desperately accumulating family wealth,

Not letting go of a single cent.

Sitting and waiting for family ruin and death,

Why not save the country and save friends?

Save the country and save friends,

To avoid being subjected to insults and disgrace!

Popular Science

A Method for Engraving Words and Pictures on Glass 179

Lai

First dissolve yellow wax and place it on the glass, making sure it is flat. After it dries, use a needle on the yellow wax to write or draw whatever you want, keeping the needle tip close to the glass.

Once the engraving process is complete, take a tin or copper container (do not use a porcelain basin) and take a small amount of silver stone powder and acid powder, purchased from a pharmacy, and mix them in the basin. At that time, a chemical reaction will occur and it will dissolve involuntarily.

While this is happening, take the engraved glass and place the yellow wax side over the medicine basin. After a short time, take it up, peel off the yellow wax, and the glass with the engraved words and pictures will be finished.

Street Sociology

Varieties of Lifestyles (6) Apricot 180

Gambling is almost the main entertainment of "city dwellers". Mahjong, poker, pai gow, dice, betting on flower meetings, guessing poetry riddles in hotels, clubs, and so-called "villas," all kinds of endless and countless patterns, all night long, night after day, is already unnecessary to say, that is, on any road, in any alley, if you are happy, you can find gambling entertainment at any time. Various "entertainments" are absolutely open and unbridled, especially for underage children. It almost seems to be recognized as a "legitimate" and "excellent" "early childhood education."

On the road or at the entrance of an alley, we can almost always see an old man with a sallow complexion or a child carrying a wooden frame. A wooden plate on the frame displays some chicken eggs, preserved plums, and sugar, etc. Another bowl contains four dice. You drop a copper coin and can throw the dice. Of course, your opponent is the owner of the wooden plate. If you roll a "one" and your opponent rolls a "two," you lose. Conversely, you win and can get three pieces of sugar or a chicken egg. If your gambling purpose is money rather than food, according to the rules, "one pays three," that is, you only lose one coin, but he pays you three.

There is also the same wooden frame, with a plate on the frame painted with red, black, and white markings. The owner of the wooden plate holds three round cardboard pieces of red, black, and white in his hand and quickly shuffles them back and forth, constantly shouting, "Look, look clearly!" He quickly covers a cardboard piece under a bowl, and then the surrounding gamblers bet and guess. If the red cardboard is covered under the bowl, and you bet on red, you win. According to the rules, it is also "one pays three."

There is also a child carrying a wooden board on his back, with round holes arranged on the board. Some holes contain a piece of sugar, a cigarette, or a few peanuts, but most are empty. The holes are all sealed with paper. You drop a copper coin and can arbitrarily poke a hole. Whatever is in the hole is your prize. If there is nothing in the hole, the copper coin is sacrificed in vain.

There are also shooting targets with air guns, drawing sugar, various patterns, different everywhere, but everywhere.

Shanghai is a world of gambling. Many people use it as a livelihood, many people use it as entertainment, and for most people, they regard it as legitimate "social education" or "early childhood education."

East, South, West, North

Magic Text 181

It was in the afternoon the other day! I happened to pass by the City God Temple and saw something that I found very interesting, so I made a note of it and shared it with the readers of the local supplement; it can also give you an idea of the psychology of the average young man!

The fact is this...

"Sir! Fortune and blessing, savior of suffering! Please have pity on me, I haven't had anything to eat all day, give me a copper coin!" A pitiful-looking beggar woman followed a young man wearing a very handsome western-style coat, crying and saying as she followed.

"Go away, go further away!" The young man answered harshly, walking his way without turning his head, but the beggar woman still called, "Sir, sir," following him for a long way. I looked at this situation and was very unhappy. I thought, can't this young man spare even a copper coin? Or perhaps he didn't have any copper coins with him? It was also possible...

I was guessing wildly when suddenly I saw this young man take a large handful of copper coins out of his purse, about a dozen or twenty, and with a rustling sound he threw them into the beggar woman's broken basket... Then I heard him say...

"You people with no clothes and no food are so pitiful!... Go, go." And so this beggar woman bent over and left with a thousand thanks.

"Ah, strange!" I was stunned by him. This young man was so stingy before, he was simply someone who wouldn't give up a single hair; why is he now generously giving away wealth? This puzzle is really difficult to solve!

Dear readers! Do you think it's strange? Haha, it turned out to be like this;

It turned out that two fashionable women were coming in front, their clothes were extremely fashionable and gorgeous. When this young man saw them, he took the opportunity to pretend to be generous and charitable to show them, actually sacrificing a dozen or twenty copper coins, and even saying some sickeningly kind words, which could be considered a great show of himself!

I turned back to look at those two women again, and sure enough, they looked at this young man, and seemed to approve of his actions as "rare and valuable!"

"Ah! The psychology of young people is originally like this." I couldn't help but exclaim again at the time

Ah!

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (16) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 182

× Government Troops Attack the County Seat

Although the Su-Song-Tai Daotai escaped into the concession under the protection of foreigners, he feared being charged by the Qing court with the serious crime of losing the city and dereliction of duty, so he planned to recover the city. At that time, government troops were stationed near the Suzhou River near the New Gate Bridge. It would not have been difficult to capture the city, but the foreigners in the concession provided a lot of assistance to the Small Swords Society, and the supplies were very abundant, so they could not be captured for a while.

Wu Jianzhang purchased a small boat, equipped it with small cannons, and led several warships from Songjiang to bombard the city on the twelfth, hoping to destroy the city walls, but the firepower was too weak and ultimately ineffective.

Government troops learned that the Small Swords Society had purchased and stored a large number of munitions in a foreign firm in the concession, so they decided to rush into the concession to seize these munitions. They dispatched a small team of government troops to rush to the customs to retrieve the munitions, but several sailors from the British warship "Spartan" came to stop them, and they were unable to retrieve them.

The Su-Song-Tai Daotai wanted to use the power of the foreigners in the concession to drive the Small Swords Society out of the city, but the foreigners were enjoying the "watching the fire from the other side" and secretly assisted the Small Swords Society quite a bit, so they took the pretext of neutrality and did not help. In fact, this attitude of neutrality was unreliable. For commercial reasons, foreigners still traded with both sides as usual.

The battlefield between the government troops and the Small Swords Society was close to the western part of the concession, and stray bullets often flew into the boundary, causing great panic among the residents. Renji Hospital on Shandong Road, founded by Dr. Lockhart, was in the line of fire, but fortunately it was spared from looting. The wounded soldiers on both sides were sent to the hospital for treatment. Foreigners going to West Shanghai were often beaten by soldiers, and the area around the New Park and the Racecourse (now Lloyd Road) became a dangerous area.

× Founding the Merchant Corps

At that time, government troops were stationed in barracks along the Suzhou River, and the Small Swords Society was in the city. Both sides' soldiers were dissatisfied with the foreigners. The imperialists in the concession wanted to take advantage of this good opportunity to expand the strength of the concession, so on the twelfth day of the fourth month of Xianfeng three years, they convened a general meeting of all residents. All the consuls and military officers of the three contracting countries, Britain, America, and France, attended. British Consul Alcock presided over the meeting and decided to implement armed neutrality, so they began to organize a merchant corps. They also appointed French military officer Tronchon, Colonel of the 2nd Battalion of Infantry, as commander, and began training that day. From then on, the imperialists had a solid military force within the concession to maintain their special interests.

Market News 183

A letter from the Shanghai Fufeng Society to our newspaper states that they are experts in newspaper collections and specialize in selling complete copies of various newspapers and supplementing various missing publications. If anyone from all walks of life has commissions, please send a letter to Li Tangli, No. 9 Dixiwei Road. Our society will sincerely serve you.

A letter from the Wuzhou Pharmacy states that the artificial blood produced by our company is indeed effective in nourishing the blood and strengthening the body. It is especially effective to take it in the cold weather. All kinds of soaps and scented soaps are sold at cost to show our determination to serve the community. Other cosmetics, medical supplies, daily necessities, etc., are now being given away as a reward to customers. Anyone who purchases goods for more than one yuan will receive a picture of a beautiful woman, and those who purchase goods for more than five yuan will receive a set of famous painting calendars.

A letter from the famous painter Wu Zaoxue states that Wu Zaoxue from Wuxing has been studying painting for more than 30 years, but he is unwilling to appear in the world due to his trivial skills, so he is rarely known. Now, due to the fact that the funeral of his three generations has not been buried, the heart of his son is uneasy. He intends to use the power of painting to widely connect with literary circles. Please send the collection address to Mr. Li Dingshi of the Huimin Company on Wangping Street. The fees will be sent immediately upon request.
